League of Nations Meeting Today, Will Surely Pass Peacefully, Italian-Ethiopian Case Will Return to Mediation 17

(Paris) It is generally believed here that the League of Nations Council meeting on Wednesday will surely pass peacefully and listen to Italy and Ethiopia negotiate a solution before August 25. Observers now believe that this dispute will still be handled by the Mediation Committee, but they believe that the real mediators are actually British Minister without Portfolio Eden and French Prime Minister and Foreign Minister Laval. Eden will pass here today on his way to Geneva, and Laval will meet with him. At the same time, according to a Reuters telegram from Geneva, all sectors related to the League of Nations believe that the result of the meeting on Wednesday will depend on Britain's attitude. Judging from the current situation, Britain does not seem to agree to simply hand the dispute over to the Mediation Committee. There is no doubt that France is willing to postpone the matter for a week, but everyone feels that if Britain advocates it first, France will surely agree. It is generally believed that the League of Nations Council is unlikely to hold public meetings for a day or two this time, given the possibility of serious consequences. It will probably hold private talks to seek a common position. (30th, Reuters)

(Rome) The Italian delegation has departed for Geneva tonight, and Italy's participation in the League of Nations Council emergency meeting has become a certainty. However, it is still difficult to predict what attitude they will take in Geneva. Well-informed sources here say that Italy's attitude will depend on the development of the League of Nations debate. Italian officials believe that the League of Nations debate should be limited to deciding on future mediation procedures. Italy will probably be defended by a number of lawyers and experts. The leader of the delegation is Sir Aorosi. (29th, National Telegram)

(Geneva) The current chairman of the League of Nations Council, Soviet Foreign Commissar Litvinov, will arrive here this afternoon. The Italian delegation will arrive tomorrow morning. The delegation includes many legal experts. Montagna and Matiko, the Italian members of the Italian-Ethiopian Mixed Arbitration Committee, are also among them. Polish Foreign Minister Beck and Czech Foreign Minister Benes will not attend. The Small Entente countries will be represented by Czech Envoy to Switzerland Silesky, while Czech Envoy to France Ususky will represent the Czech government. As for the British chief representative, Minister without Portfolio Eden, he will pass through Paris today and meet with French Prime Minister and Foreign Minister Laval before arriving here by the same car tonight. The first meeting of the Council is scheduled to be held at 5:00 pm tomorrow. In addition, this special session of the Council is somewhat secret in nature and may not be fully open to the public. (30th, Havas Telegram)

Eden Meets French Premier 18

(London) Minister without Portfolio Anthony Eden flew from here to Paris at 12:30 today, arriving in the French capital at 2:45 PM. He will go to the French Foreign Ministry at 5:00 PM to meet with French Premier and Foreign Minister Laval. (Havas dispatch, 30th)

(London) British cabinet member Eden departed by plane at 12:30 this afternoon. According to reliable sources, the British delegation is heading to Geneva without a fixed resolution on the attitude that Britain should adopt. Eden has the authority to make a plan according to the circumstances. However, it is expected that Eden's conversation with French Premier Laval in Paris this afternoon will allow Britain and France to reach an understanding on this attitude. It is likely that these statesmen will travel together to Geneva to attend the League of Nations Executive Council meeting tomorrow evening to discuss the Italian-Abyssinian dispute. According to custom, the first meeting of the Executive Council is not open to the public so that participants can draft an agenda. It is expected that before the meeting, Executive Council Chairman Litvinov, Laval, Eden, and Italian chief representative Aloisi will hold private talks. There are two key points in Britain's policy on the Italian-Abyssinian issue: one is to maintain peace, and the other is to uphold the authority of the League of Nations, as the League is the mechanism by which countries undertake to submit their disputes for resolution. The exchange of views between Britain and France has proven that the same is also the French government's objective. As for the procedures to be adopted in handling this matter, it will be decided by the League of Nations Executive Council. The general opinion, especially in Paris, is that a slight delay may be beneficial to the matter, as this period of hesitation may provide an opportunity for continued mediation, and the financial and economic impacts after the outbreak of war may also be factors in preventing war. It is widely believed that the Executive Council meeting will ask the Mediation Committee to continue its efforts to seek a resolution. If no result is achieved by August 25, the League of Nations will appoint a fifth arbitrator. (Reuters dispatch, 30th)

(London) According to well-informed sources, the British representative attending the League of Nations Executive Council meeting has been instructed by the government, before departing for Geneva, to adopt all possible means to resolve the dispute between Italy and Abyssinia in accordance with the spirit of the League of Nations Covenant. However, Britain maintains its original position, namely that the scope of the Executive Council's discussion should not be limited to the Walwal incident, but should be a comprehensive exploration of the issue of Italian-Abyssinian relations. If this procedure is adopted, the Executive Council may entrust the representatives of Britain, France, and Italy to seek a compromise within the framework of the League of Nations, in accordance with the 1906 Tripartite Treaty regarding Abyssinia. However, it should be noted that neither Italy nor Abyssinia should take advantage of this period of negotiations to engage in military preparations. To this end, Britain hopes that Italy will promise not to engage in war during the negotiation period. (Havas dispatch, 29th)

Danish Farmers Petition 27

Copenhagen 50,000 Danish farmers held an orderly demonstration in front of the palace, urging the King to pay attention to the plight of the farmers. The King met with a representative of the farmers in front of Stenning. The representative presented a petition requesting that agriculture receive the same protection as other economic sectors of the country. The King stated that, according to the constitution, he had no right to express an opinion on this matter, so the representative should ask the Prime Minister to pay attention to the farmers' difficulties. The representative then met with the Prime Minister for half an hour, but finally told the waiting crowd that the government's proposed guarantees were not satisfactory, as they would only delay the matter. American Recovery Achievements 28

(New York) According to economic statistics released here today, the economic decline in the United States has now come to an end. The evidence for this is as follows: (1) The total value of American stocks traded on the New York Stock Exchange increased from US$15 billion during the worst of the economic panic in 1933 to US$300 billion in 1934, and now to US$37 billion. At the same time, the total value of domestic public debt listed on the New York Stock Exchange has also increased by US$7.5 billion since the lowest point in 1933. Therefore, the total price of stocks and public debt has now increased by US$30 billion compared to before, a figure not much different from the current total national debt, and far exceeding the cost of the New Deal. (2) Automobile sales in the first half of the year increased by 31% compared to the same period last year. (3) Steel industry production is also more active than before. (4) Construction in the first half of the year increased by 51% compared to the same period last year. (5) Electricity industry production in the first half of the year increased by 7% compared to the same period last year. (6) Bank clearing increased by 8%. (7) The total value of agricultural products this year is US$8.5 billion, an increase of US$1 billion compared to last year. (8) The total profit of various commercial firms in the first half of the year increased by 2% compared to the same period last year. (National News Agency dispatch, 29th)

American Gold and Silver Mine District Congressmen Oppose Wealth Tax Bill 29

(Washington) Congressmen representing the western gold and silver mining regions, seeing that President Roosevelt's wealth tax bill greatly harms the interests of the western gold and silver mining industry, have risen up to oppose the bill. Nevada Democratic Congressman Heron argues that the excess profits tax in the bill will greatly harm the interests of the gold and silver mining industry, so he asked the Senate Finance Committee to reconsider the bill before submitting it to the House of Representatives, but the Finance Committee replied that it was too late to save. Therefore, Heron has asked the silver-supporting congressmen in the House of Representatives to meet on Tuesday morning to discuss adding amendments. It is said that this amendment is roughly the same as the one added to the financial bill in 1918, namely that the profits of the gold and silver mining industry are exempt from the excess profits tax. (National Telegram, 29th)

International Commercial Telegram

—Special Commercial Report from Reuters, July 30—

Gold and Silver

British Gold: The London gold price today is 140 shillings and 5 pence, down 2 pence.

British Silver: The London silver market is quiet. The spot price is 30 pence and 1875, and the futures price is 30 pence and 25, both unchanged. China sold, the United States bought, and the market is stable.

American Silver: The Mount Airy silver market is stable. The opening price for September futures rose 20 pounds to 67.90 to 68.05.

Exchange Rates

British-American: The London foreign exchange market was relatively quiet this morning. The opening price for British-American exchange was 4 dollars, 96 cents, and 125, the same as yesterday's closing price for American-British. Within the first hour, it fell by 1875 to 4 dollars, 95 cents, and 9375. It continued to fall by 125 at noon to 4 dollars, 95 cents, and 8125. This price was maintained until 2:00 PM.

British-French: The opening price was unchanged at 75 francs and 06. After the first hour, it fell by 9 pounds to 74 francs and 97, and there were no further changes.

Cotton and Wheat

American Cotton: The cotton market opened unchanged, trading was sluggish, and prices were unchanged, as merchants were unwilling to make any new purchases.

British Wheat: The Liverpool wheat market continued to weaken today. At 1:00 PM, the price for October futures fell by 2 pence to 5 shillings, 1 pence, and 75.

British Cotton: The Liverpool cotton market tended to fall this morning. At 1:00 PM, the price for October futures was 6.18, down 3 pounds.

American Wheat: The Chicago wheat and grain markets both opened slightly lower. Later, the wheat market tended to decline, while grains were stable. It is expected that the Canadian grain market will hinder the creation of new buying sentiment here.

Rubber

London: The rubber market was stable at the opening, but later turned light. At noon, the trading price for October-December futures was 5 pence and 875, up 0.0625 from yesterday's close.

New York: The rubber market was relatively stable today. It opened up about 7 pounds, but later turned quiet.

Securities

New York: The securities market opened weak this morning, prices were still stable, but later, due to profit-taking by bulls, it presented a mixed picture, with very slight price fluctuations. The Dow Jones 30 Industrial Average was 126.57, up 1 pound.

British and German Journalists Kidnapped East of Zhangbei and Baochang: German Journalist Muller Released 33

(Beiping) British journalist Jones and German journalist Muller were kidnapped yesterday in the area east of Zhangbei and Baochang. After receiving the report, Qin Decun, Chairman of Chahar Province, who is recuperating in Beiping, telegraphed the Chahar Provincial Government to investigate the truth as soon as possible and find ways to rescue them quickly. According to related sources, the incident occurred in Baochang. The area where they were kidnapped is only maintained by local militia, whose strength may be relatively weak. This reporter visited Qin Decun this afternoon, but Qin was unable to meet due to illness. According to a person close to him, the Zhangjiakou telephone reported this matter this morning, stating that the British man Jones and the German man Muller held passports to travel to Erlian on the Zhangku Highway within Outer Mongolia, and were traveling by Deutsch-Asiatische Petroleum Gesellschaft car to Bailingmiao, Beile Temple, and other places. Then they went to Duolun. Yesterday, they took the original car back to Zhangjiakou, but did not take the Zhangduo highway, but instead took the dirt road to the northeast, heading south. When they traveled to Guanmazhou, 50 li northeast of Baochang, they were suddenly robbed by bandits. This is the correct official report obtained from Zhangyuan. It has been found that the foreign affairs of Chahar have just begun. The area of Baochang and Guyuan is maintained by a small number of security teams. The security teams have recently entered the area and are not familiar with the local situation, while the Guanmazhou area is close to the border line, with barren grass and sparse population, and there are no security teams. The two British and German journalists risked going deep, which led to the kidnapping incident. The provincial government has ordered the county magistrates of Baochang and Zhan Yuan and the security team leader to quickly dispatch personnel to investigate and search, hoping to cooperate in rescuing them as soon as possible. According to a spokesman for the British Embassy, after the embassy received a report that Jones had been kidnapped in the area east of Baochang, it telegraphed Ambassador Knatchbull-Hugessen, who is currently vacationing in Beidaihe, for instructions. At the same time, the embassy has notified the Beiping Military Branch to find ways to assist in the rescue. Military Attaché Shaw of the embassy is currently traveling in Outer Mongolia and has been telegraphed to ask him not to return to Beiping for the time being, and to go to Zhangyuan to cooperate with the Chahar Provincial Government in making every effort to rescue them. A spokesman for the German Embassy stated that German Ambassador Trautmann is currently vacationing in Beidaihe. The embassy has telegraphed the ambassador about Muller's kidnapping and has also notified the Beiping and Chahar provincial authorities separately, requesting them to find ways to rescue him as soon as possible. During the rescue period, the embassy does not intend to make any further statements. (Special dispatch, 30th)

(Beiping) The German journalist kidnapped in Chahar was released by the bandits on the 30th and will arrive in Zhangyuan on the 31st. The British journalist has not yet been released. The British Embassy has sent Counselor Sahanman to visit Wang Kemin at 10:00 AM on the 31st, asking him to expedite the rescue. It is reported that the bandits have put forward conditions, demanding 100,000 yuan and 200 automatic pistols. (Special dispatch, 30th)

(Beiping) According to a telegram from Zhangyuan this afternoon, Dr. Muller, a German journalist who was seized by bandits in Baochang on Saturday, has been released. It is reported that Muller is currently traveling by car to Zhangyuan, but Jones, who was also seized, is still being held. The British Embassy in China has lodged representations with the Ministry of Foreign Affairs in Nanjing and the Beiping Military Branch today. Qin Decun, Chairman of Chahar, is currently in Beiping. It is said that he has telegraphed the county magistrates of Baochang and Zhangyuan to find ways to rescue them. Jones is currently being held in the mountains northeast of Baochang. The Russian chauffeur and a Chinese servant who escaped from the bandits have now arrived in Zhangyuan. According to them, the kidnapping took place at Guanmakou (transliteration), 15 li northeast of Baochang. (Reuters dispatch, 30th)

Dutch East Indies Anti-Chinese Issue: Diplomatic Negotiations. The Focus of Negotiations is on Overseas Chinese Laws and Immigration Restrictions. The Dutch Side Has Already Provided a Formal Response on the Issue of Legal Treatment. 67

The Dutch East Indies has been actively implementing economic exclusion measures to resist foreign economic forces, particularly against overseas Chinese residing in the Dutch East Indies. This is because the number of Chinese residing in the Dutch East Indies is large, and their economic gains have been greatly harmed by these exclusionary measures. Since June of this year, hundreds of overseas Chinese residing in the Dutch East Indies have been forced to return to China due to these exclusionary measures, damaging the development of overseas Chinese trade. After receiving reports, the Chinese government instructed Jin Wensi, the Chinese envoy to the Netherlands, to negotiate with the Dutch Foreign Minister de Graeff and actively engage in talks. It is learned that Envoy Jin has recently submitted a report to the Chinese government detailing the negotiation process, which provides a detailed account of the two major issues of legal status for overseas Chinese and Dutch East Indies immigration restrictions. The details of this report, as well as the Chinese government's note to the Dutch Foreign Ministry and the Dutch Foreign Ministry's recent note to Envoy Jin, are recorded below.

Issue of Restricting Immigration of Overseas Chinese 68

Over 1.2 million overseas Chinese have gathered in the Dutch East Indies. The economic undertakings they operate not only occupy an important position there but also have a significant relationship with the domestic economy. Therefore, the relationship between China and the Netherlands is becoming increasingly complex, and all issues between the two countries must be resolved quickly and well to strengthen friendly relations. Since 1933, the Dutch East Indies has been affected by the global economic panic and proposed immigration restriction measures the year before last as a means of relief. The contents of the measures include: (1) Specifying the total annual immigration quota, which was set at 12,000 people for both last year and this year, to be evenly distributed among 15 nationalities; (2) If the number of entries does not reach the quota, the number of immigrants may be increased by each nationality, but may not exceed one-tenth of the total number of immigrants of that nationality to the Dutch East Indies during the ten consecutive years before the implementation of the new regulations; (3) After the quota limit is reached, only nationalities whose immigration quota has not been reached will be allowed to continue to immigrate until the limit is reached. When this regulation was first submitted to the Dutch East Indies National Assembly, all levels of Chinese society believed that if the regulation were passed and implemented, not only would the Chinese policy of emigration to the south be hit, but also the existing economic position of overseas Chinese in the Dutch East Indies would be fatally shaken. According to the average number of Chinese entering the country from 1923 to 1932, the annual average was approximately 29,200 people. Even according to the average from 1929 to 1932, the annual average was approximately 16,900 people. If the new immigration regulations are followed, the legal quota for Chinese immigrants each year would be only 800 people. Therefore, after the Chinese people heard this news, public opinion was turbulent and resentment was widespread. The former acting representative of the Chinese embassy in the Netherlands submitted very simple notes to the Dutch Foreign Ministry on June 29th and August 22nd of the same year, urging it to consider the status of overseas Chinese in the Dutch East Indies and to prevent the regulation from being passed hastily. Unfortunately, the Dutch East Indies National Assembly passed the immigration regulation on September 6th of the same year, and the Dutch government also approved it. After Envoy Jin Wensi took office, he repeatedly negotiated with the Dutch Foreign Ministry and urged it to respond as soon as possible. On December 4th, 1933, he sent a new note (original text attached) to the Dutch Foreign Ministry, explaining the government's views in detail based on the economic history and relationship of overseas Chinese in the Dutch East Indies, their commercial status, and the unequal impact of the implementation of the new regulations on overseas Chinese. He urged the Dutch government to change its attitude and declared that it reserved the right to raise this issue again in the future. At the same time, he hoped that the Governor-General of the Dutch East Indies would consider China's views when setting the annual immigration quota and requested that it adopt necessary measures to ensure that the provisions of Section 18, Item B, Section 1 of the new regulations could be implemented and that the statements made by the Dutch government representatives in the National Assembly could be fulfilled.

Issue of Equal Legal Treatment 69

Article 163 of the Dutch East Indies Constitution stipulates that all Europeans, Americans, Japanese, and those born in other countries whose family laws are the same as Dutch law are collectively referred to as Europeans. Chinese and Arabs are collectively referred to as Eastern Foreign Residents. There are many points of unequal treatment. The most notable is that cases involving Europeans are tried by judges who are proficient in law, while this is not the case for Eastern Foreign Residents. Also, in criminal cases, Europeans are arrested by the court according to law, while Eastern Foreign Residents are arrested and detained by the police station. The facilities and treatment enjoyed by European detention centers and prisons are also superior to those of Eastern Foreign Residents. For these unequal treatments, our overseas Chinese have endured them for hundreds of years. After the success of the Northern Expedition of the Revolutionary Army and the establishment of the National Government in Nanjing, the foundation of unification was somewhat stabilized. The former Dutch Governor, Mr. Anobies Cornelis Dirk De Graef, the current Dutch Foreign Minister, stated in his speech at the opening of the 11th regular session of the National Assembly on June 15th, 1929: "The government of the Republic of China will promulgate a family law on January 1st of next year. If it can be implemented, the overseas Chinese in the Dutch East Indies can be treated equally with the Dutch in law." However, the family law promulgated by our country was implemented successively from May 5th, 1931, succeeding various laws in the 20th year of the Republic. The legal treatment of our overseas Chinese in the Dutch East Indies has not yet been equal to that of Europeans, Americans, and Japanese. Therefore, our country's diplomatic authorities stationed in the Netherlands have continued to negotiate with the Dutch government, hoping that overseas Chinese can obtain equal legal treatment. Recently, the Dutch Foreign Ministry sent a note to our country's embassy in the Netherlands on May 2nd of last year, stating that regarding the legal status of our country's overseas Chinese, except for the fact that the criminal procedure law still needs to be improved, in terms of civil law, civil procedure law, commercial law, and criminal law, they can be considered to be treated the same as Europeans. Envoy Jin reported this to the ministry and instructed Consul General Song in Batavia to conduct a thorough investigation, which confirmed that this was the actual situation. However, this matter still requires further effort in order to achieve satisfactory results. It is hoped that the people of the country will pay close attention to it at all times. (To be continued)

Local News

Industry and Commerce Revitalization Council: Leaders of Various Industries Talk 78

First Complete the Investigation Report on 43 Industries. Invite Leaders of Various Industries as Advisory Committee Members. 79

Since its establishment, the Industry and Commerce Revitalization Council has been discussing the causes of the decline of industry and commerce and formulating revitalization plans. The deputy directors of the investigation team, Xi Yushu and Xu Xiaochu, together with the deputy chairmen of the committee, Wang Yansong and Jin Runxiang, and the deputy directors of various groups, Zhang Naiqi, Luo Qinghua, Yan Miaosheng, and Ren Jinping, have been meeting with leaders and experts from various industries according to the preliminary work procedure. Experts and leaders who have agreed to attend the meetings include Zhu Yangchen, Zhang Wuyun, Hu Juewen, Gao Shiheng, Zhou Bangjun, Zhang Huikang, Li Kangnian, Shen Weiting, Zheng Hairuo, and Ma Jisheng, among others. The opinions expressed are extremely valuable. It has been learned that Wang Yansong, the chairman of the council, has summarized the opinions of various parties and plans to first complete the investigation report on the scope of 43 industries. The content of this report focuses on two points: one is the internal and external causes of the decline of various industries, and the other is effective recommendations for rescuing the decline. At the same time, the implementation of the revitalization plan is also being planned and researched. Now, in order to speed up the completion of this report, Wang has specially sent letters to the leaders and experts of various industries, inviting them to serve as advisory committee members to jointly assist. The original letter and the list of advisory committee members are recorded below.

Letter of Appointment 80

Dear Sir, Since the attack of the economic panic has invaded our China, because the domestic industries have not had a sound organization, they have felt painful in self-defense. As a result, the phenomena of rural collapse, industrial and commercial decline, and financial turbulence have formed one after another. If we do not take this opportunity to rise up and strive for struggle, not only will we not be able to survive, but also the disaster of national subjugation and genocide will be inevitable. The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce, in view of this, organized this association based on the resolution of the Sixth Congress, in order to fulfill its responsibilities. However, this matter is of great importance and cannot be achieved overnight. It is necessary to gather experts widely, thoroughly explore the causes of the disease, and determine the plan. Then, the work can be carried out effectively. I have long admired you as the leader of an industry. Regarding the key to the decline of the industry and the development plan, you will not hesitate to impart your knowledge and guidance. Therefore, I am writing to invite you to serve as an advisory committee member of this association. I hope that you will be mindful of the national crisis and generously assist. This is my sincere hope.

American Educator Dr. Schmitt Talks About How Americans Do Not Want War; Came to Shanghai to Investigate the Situation in the Far East 84

The China Press reports that American educator Dr. Schmitt believes that the United States' Far East policy is of utmost importance given the current situation, so he has come to the Far East to investigate everything on the ground. Dr. Schmitt has been a professor of modern history and chairman of the history department at the University of Chicago since 1925. He will stay in China for at least two months to investigate what he calls the "real situation." Dr. Schmitt is one of the leading historical writers in the United States today and is the author of "The Coming of the War", published in 1930. In 1931 he won the Pulitzer Prize for History. After touring Japan for a month, he took a short trip to Hong Kong and Manila and arrived in Shanghai on Sunday (the 28th). A representative of the China Press visited him. According to him, although many people in the United States are worried about war, they all earnestly hope not to be dragged into any war. Dr. Schmitt personally does not believe that war cannot be avoided, and said that if a war breaks out in the Far East, it will definitely be between Russia and Japan, not between Japan and the United States.

Lawyer Raven and Mr. Evans Protest to Mr. Hefford; Trial of the Case Will Be Held Around September or October 86

The China Press reports that on Monday, Raven's lawyer, Mr. Evans, on behalf of Raven and the staff of the three companies formerly run by Raven that are currently being liquidated, sent a public letter to Mr. Hefford, the liquidator of the American Oriental Banking Corporation, protesting against the statements made by Mr. Hefford to news reporters regarding the handling of affairs of the related companies, saying that they impede the collection of rent by Probst, Hanbury & Co., Ltd., and the liquidation of the other three companies. Although Mr. Hefford is responsible for speaking frankly without fear, it is hoped that in the future he will speak purely on facts and not criticize the former employees of the companies. The letter also refutes Mr. Hefford's claims that the American Oriental Banking Corporation was already empty and on the verge of bankruptcy before the liquidation, and that the bank's failure had nothing to do with the Shanghai monetary crunch. It states that Mr. Hefford should check the accounts of the American Oriental Banking Corporation, American Eastern Banking Corporation, Probst, Hanbury & Co., Ltd., and Probst, Hanbury & Co., Ltd., at the end of December 1934 to know the actual shares of the companies at that time. Near the end of 1934, the American Oriental Banking Corporation's cash reserves, as a proportion of deposits, were likely higher than those of other banks. Later, due to the monetary crunch, depositors rushed to withdraw money, resulting in the emptying of cash reserves. The fixed deposits of the other three companies, after maturity in previous years, were mostly renewed, accounting for 75% of the total. In the winter of 1934 and 1935, due to the extremely tight monetary situation, it was impossible to borrow cash from banks even with reliable securities as collateral. Therefore, depositors, needing money urgently, did not renew their deposits after maturity, and the three companies had to do their best to collect cash to meet the withdrawal of deposits. Their assets had not decreased compared to the past, and the total amount of their liabilities had not increased. When the companies were in urgent need, they had to borrow cash from the American Oriental Banking Corporation with their securities as collateral. Although the bank may not have lent money based on the shares of its affiliated companies, this is another issue entirely and should not be referred to as fraud or bankruptcy. The directors of the companies are all representatives of Shanghai's business community and are responsible. It seems unlikely that they would try to maintain a failing business or commit fraud. The letter was personally delivered to the representatives of the newspapers by Raven. Mr. Evans, after writing the letter, returned to Tianjin last Saturday and will come to Shanghai again when Raven's trial is scheduled. The trial of the case will probably not begin until around September or October, because Mr. Hefford's lawyer, Mr. Schletter, and Raven's lawyer, Mr. Evans, need time to prepare their arguments.

Yu Qiaqing Talks About Deciding to Resign as Chairman of the Shipping Association; Difficult to Compete with Japanese Ships; Joint Transportation Has Only Lip Service; Great Pain and Mixed Feelings; Resigning to Apologize 87

Since the news of Mr. Yu Qiaqing's letter of resignation from the positions of standing committee member and chairman of the Shanghai Shipping Association and standing director of the China Shipping Cooperative Society was reported, a reporter from the New Voice News Agency specially visited Mr. Yu at the Sanbei Company to inquire about everything. Mr. Yu was kind enough to express his views as follows: I went to Japan to observe military exercises in the 16th year of the Guangxu reign of the Qing Dynasty. After returning to China, seeing the rapid progress of the Meiji Restoration and the assistance of Prime Minister Ito and Viscount Shibusawa to the government, I was moved. Because I am a businessman, and the shipping industry is the crown of all businesses, and imitating Shibusawa's management of the Nippon Yusen Kaisha, I was determined to manage the shipping industry. The shipping industry is essential for the circulation of goods and convenient transportation, and it is also a powerful tool for military transportation in case of emergency. For forty years, I have been earnestly working towards this goal without懈怠. The steps I took were to first operate domestic shipping routes and then try to develop international shipping routes. Therefore, I founded Ning Shao, acquired Hong An, and operated the Sanbei and Ning Xing companies. However, the idea of international shipping routes has never been forgotten. Because there were few like-minded compatriots at that time, I expanded by borrowing money. I not only adhered to the above-mentioned principles, but also sought livelihoods for the majority of employees. I never considered my own interests. During that time, I repeatedly requested the government to formulate maritime laws to protect ship owners. The current status of Chinese ship crewmen is also an undeniable fact. The Customs, which was presided over by foreign advisors, originally stipulated that ships longer than 200 feet were not allowed to employ Chinese crewmen. I used my own ships and property as collateral to fight for the gradual insertion of people with experience from the deck and engine room. Because there were no suitable people at the time, people with experience, although slightly lower in academic qualifications, were able to cope with the service. This was originally a temporary expedient. Therefore, I further sought ways out for the graduates of the first Wusong Merchant Marine School, and levied an additional 30% tonnage tax from shipping colleagues to revive the Merchant Marine School and to support the establishment of the Maritime Affairs Bureau in order to recover the maritime administration operated by the Customs on behalf of the government. All of this came from a sincere enthusiasm. I never expected the shipping industry to decline day by day. The burdens have been added layer upon layer, and I am unable to save myself, which has earned me the rebuke of "spinning a cocoon around myself." I cannot help but sigh. The Shanghai Shipping Association was established out of necessity in July of the 16th year of the Republic of China. In November of the 20th year of the Republic of China, it was reorganized into the Shipping Industry Association. Since December of the 23rd year of the Republic of China, it has been renamed the Shipping Industry Association. I have been mistakenly elected by my colleagues to serve as president, member of the presidium, and chairman of the standing committee for eight years. The matter is obligatory, and it is also related to my own interests, so I have not dared to resign. During that time, I provided military transportation for the government and fought for the sovereignty of the industry, and I was exhausted. In recent years, the collapse of the rural economy, the financial crunch, and the decline of the shipping industry are unprecedented. The Japanese ships have lower expenses and are subsidized by the government, which makes it even more difficult to compete. At this time of exhaustion, at this critical moment of survival, this is not the day I should resign. However, a hundred feelings are mixed, and there is no end to them. After the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company was nationalized and withdrew from the association, it formed a situation of confrontation between state-owned and private enterprises. Although the Provisional Constitution clearly stipulates the provisions for encouraging and protecting private shipping enterprises, they have not been realized. After several struggles for land and water combined transportation, private enterprises were allowed to receive the same treatment as state-owned enterprises by the government, but they have not yet been involved. Other measures clearly delineate boundaries. I have appealed to the government for relief for five years, but there has been only lip service, with no practical measures implemented. There is no hope of maintaining or developing. Looking back at the development of the Japanese shipping industry over the past forty years, with shipping routes all over the world, all its success lies in the cooperation between the government and the people, which has made it what it is today. How can it not be disheartening? The recovery of maritime rights and the development of international shipping routes are beyond my ability. I believe I am no longer capable of doing so. I depend on future talents. As for shipping cooperation, it is the only way to save the current difficulties and is supported by myself and all my colleagues. If it is handled impartially, it will be effective. However, the preparation and design has been going on for a year, and the establishment of the board of directors has been three months, but nothing has been done, as if it were a mere formality. I am ashamed of being a standing director, but after careful consideration of the situation and looking around the environment, the effectiveness has not been seen, and disputes have arisen again. In short, at this time, I can neither win the sympathy of the government nor live up to the expectations of my colleagues. If this continues, I will mislead myself and others, and it will become more and more serious. I can only sincerely resign from the positions of standing committee member and chairman of the Shipping Association and standing director of the Shipping Cooperative Society, and apologize to the government and my colleagues. I have already made up my mind.

Among the various sectors of Shanghai, there is no lack of benevolent people. Can they not be saddened by reading this?

Report from the Relief Commissioner The Red Swastika Society, upon receiving the news of the Yellow River breach, immediately sent a relief commissioner to the disaster areas of Ji, Jin, Yu, Zhen, and Yun counties to investigate the disaster situation. According to the report, this time the Yellow River breach, upstream on the south bank, has spread from Zhen County's Linpu gathering to He, Yun, Ju, Jia, Dong, and Wen counties. Recent measurements show that the main trend is southward, towards Shan, Ji, Ning, Jinxiang, Yutai, and then gradually entering Jiangsu Province via Tengyi. The area that has already been affected by the disaster is 300 li in both length and width, and there are more than 2 million disaster victims. At this time of entering the hot season, it is the period of continued rising water. If it continues to flow like this, it will swallow the canal and merge with the lake, not only causing disaster to southern Shandong, but also harming northern Jiangsu. If the channel is seized and the Yellow River shifts south, what a terrible change it would be. It is reported that Jiangsu Province has strengthened its defenses, and the work is very strong. It is hoped that all sectors of Jiangsu Province will cultivate good fortune, wear their hair disheveled, and coronate themselves in order to save the disaster-stricken areas. Invisibly, they can pray to avoid future disasters. Extreme poverty and calling out to heaven is the constant feeling of people. Doing good and receiving blessings is a clear instruction from ancient times.

Telegram from the Jining Red Swastika Society The flood this time is unprecedented. Our relief team set off by boat, but could only reach Jiaxiang and Juye from Jining, and could not reach Yuncheng, let alone Zhencheng. Along the way, the villages we saw, except for those that were completely washed away, had only rooftops left. Women, children, and the elderly, whether rich or poor, were either standing in the water, perched on rooftops, or gathered on broken embankments clinging to large trees, without clothes, food, or anyone to turn to, crying for help. It was unbearable to hear. The team members could not help but cry loudly at this terrible sight. Alas, who doesn't have parents, who doesn't have a wife and children? How can we not be saddened? The team members immediately gave them baked pancakes and fried noodles in the water and sent them to the receiving stations in various counties. The exact number of people and animals washed away cannot be investigated at this time because the flood has not receded. Under the hot sun, those disaster victims who cannot land are suffering from the heat, and at night they are exposed to the wind and dew. When it rains, they are covered in mud and water, and when it is sunny, their skin is scorched. If they are not rescued urgently, the living will gradually die. In the torrents and giant waves, are there not rich merchants and wealthy gentlemen, high officials and powerful gentry? Even if gold and silver are piled up like mountains, they cannot save themselves at this moment, let alone save others. From a well, you cannot save people. Now we are fortunate to be above the well, so it is a good time to save people. Saving people is saving ourselves, this is the time! Recently, more than 1,000 disaster victims who have escaped from Jining and Jiaxiang arrive at the train station every day. Our society gives each person one jin of steamed buns every morning and evening. In four days, we have boarded more than 8,000 people. It is still unknown how many more cannot get out of the water. We urge all societies to appeal to all sectors of society to send teams to the disaster areas as soon as possible, hire more boats, prepare more dry food, and bring more medicines to rush to the rescue. We sincerely cry out and beg for the disaster victims in western Shandong, and await your telegram in response.

Salvation of Black Fever Sufferers: Hope to Establish Branch Offices in Counties for Universal Relief 98

Black fever, originating from north of the Yangtze River, spreads rapidly and is often fatal. Recently, Wang Junshu, a respected gentleman from Huaiyin, Jiangsu Province, came to Shanghai to share a remarkably effective secret remedy, which has been repeatedly reported in the past and has attracted attention from all sectors, prompting generous donations of medicine. Since Mr. Wang came to Shanghai to purchase large quantities of medicine and could not stay long, he entrusted the Shanghai Chinese and Foreign Charity Relief Association on Renji Road to receive donations and help the masses. The association recently received a letter from Mr. Wang, which is transcribed below: "Received your letter and remittance of 4,400 silver dollars, which is acknowledged. The number of people seeking medicine for black fever is increasing daily, adding approximately 20 to 30 people each day, which is unstoppable. Currently, we need to administer three doses of medicine daily, and some people travel over a hundred miles to obtain it. At present it is the hot summer and it is already like this. The amount of medicine needed daily is difficult to predict. If charities can set up branch offices in each county, relief can be provided universally, and our operations will not be overwhelmed. Manufacturing the medicine is a complex process, and the honey pills must be made by hand. Entrusting a pharmacy to manufacture the medicine is unreliable, and we are concerned that they may not be able to keep up with demand. Therefore, we will look for multiple pharmacies to manufacture the medicine, which will increase labor costs and make it difficult to monitor. Currently, we are building three tin-roofed rooms in the backyard of the pharmacy to be used specifically for manufacturing the medicine. We are also building a furnace for refining copper sulfate, which will require one or two additional workers. Those who come to the pharmacy to seek medicine are divided into two categories: those who have already received medicine and those who have not. Those who have already received medicine must be asked about their condition after taking the medicine, and details must be noted on a form. Those who have not received medicine must be asked about their name, age, place of origin, address, date of onset, and symptoms, and details must be noted on a form, along with the date of medication. Each person is given four days' worth of medicine, and they must return on the fifth day to report their symptoms and effectiveness, which must be recorded on a form before another four days' worth of medicine is given. This procedure may seem tedious, but it is necessary to obtain accurate information. It would be best to ask the Red Cross to send people north to establish branch offices in each county, which would provide more widespread relief. Refining copper sulfate is the most labor-intensive part of the manufacturing process, which we can do here. The other ingredients can be mixed independently. The medicine should be mainly in the form of pills, supplemented by medicinal wine and plaster. The pills alone can cure the disease. The medicinal wine is not suitable for young children and should not be consumed in large quantities by women, so little wine is used. Two ingredients in the plaster are extremely difficult to find, and even if found, they are not available in large quantities. Therefore, we should use whatever is available. The focus should remain on the pills. Please inform the Red Cross that it would be best if many philanthropists set up offices in each county to eradicate this disease." This letter was from Wang Bao-huai. It is reported that the association has conveyed this to the Red Cross, hoping that they can find a way to establish branch offices in each county to provide universal relief to the people. Although there are people who continue to donate money and medicine, the road ahead is long, and the need for funds is vast. It is hoped that philanthropists will work together to maintain this effort, and that many hands will make light work.

After the Sinking of the Xin Maoli Steamer: No Proper Arrangements for the Victims; Dinghai Fellow Townsmen in Shanghai Meet to Discuss Solutions 99

The Xin Maoli steamer sank at the Dinghai Wharf on July 13. The tragic deaths of the passengers and the circumstances of the rescue were detailed in the Dinghai Zhou Newspaper. Over half a month has passed, and the shipping company has made no statement regarding its responsibility for the tragedy, nor has it announced any arrangements for the aftermath. The Dinghai Fellow Townsmen Association in Shanghai believes that since the accident occurred in Dinghai and many of the victims were from Taizhou and Dinghai, it is inappropriate to remain silent. Therefore, a 14th Standing Committee Meeting was convened on Monday, July 29, to discuss solutions. The attending members were Yuan Yang'an, Chen Gengxin (representing Yuan Yang'an), Pan Shanglin, Zhu Baofeng (representing Pan Shanglin), and Zhou Xiangsheng. The attendees were Ding Zihua, Lu Ruixing, Chen Dafang, Jiang Xinzhao (Jiang Mengyun), Le Nanting, and Hu Zhizhai. Yuan Yang'an chaired the meeting, and Hu Zhizhai recorded the minutes. (A) Report Items: The chairman reported the purpose of the meeting, followed by Jiang Mengyun's report on the sinking of the Xin Maoli steamer, citing three reasons: 1. The steamer was a used vessel purchased from abroad. 2. The cargo was loaded too high, making it top-heavy. 3. The doors were too low, making it easy for water to enter. He said that before the voyage, he had visited the ship and specialists had already noted the various dangers. The Maritime Administration, as the governing body, ignored these points. If the steamer had been thoroughly inspected, this tragedy would not have occurred. Therefore, this tragedy was not an act of God but entirely man-made. (B) Discussion Items: What should be done regarding the Xin Maoli steamer tragedy? Resolutions: 1. Send a letter to the Dinghai County Government to investigate thoroughly. 2. Send personnel to Dinghai to investigate the truth. 3. Petition the Ministry of Communications to send personnel to investigate thoroughly. 4. Work together with the Taizhou Fellow Townsmen Association in Shanghai to handle the matter. 5. Organize a tragedy committee to be responsible for handling the matter. Chen Dafang, Lu Shoulun, Shen Rongan, Zhou Xiangsheng, Pan Shanglin, Jiang Mengyun, and Yuan Yang'an were appointed as committee members. It was also decided that a special committee discussion would be held this Wednesday (July 31).

Chinese Institute of Engineers Awards Honorary Gold Medal to Hou Debang 102

Hou Debang, the chief engineer of the Yongli Alkali Factory in Tanggu, Tianjin, has been in charge of the factory's engineering affairs for over a decade. He is the author of "The Manufacture of Soda," a monograph of the American Chemical Society and recognized by chemical experts worldwide as a rare masterpiece on chemical engineering. As a member of the Chinese Institute of Engineers, the association, based on its regulations for awarding honorary gold medals, appointed experts from the board and executive departments to conduct a detailed review. All agreed that Mr. Hou's work has been praised by Western industrial experts and domestic engineering scholars alike. The book elucidates new principles, promotes specialized knowledge, and benefits humanity and engineering. Therefore, it was decided to award him the 1935 Honorary Gold Medal in recognition of his contributions.

Shanghai Municipal Council's Reasons for Not Prosecuting the Da Zhonghua Case 103

Regarding the fire at the Da Zhonghua Celluloid Factory on Xiaoshadu Road last month, which caused extensive damage and spread to nearby residences, there have been inquiries about whether the Shanghai Municipal Council has taken any action. The explosion and fire at the factory were a major incident, resulting in 25 deaths and 44 injuries. The Shanghai Municipal Council is deeply concerned about this matter, but it has not been able to take any legal action. According to the Criminal Procedure Law of the Republic of China, if the injured parties file a private prosecution, the local authorities cannot simultaneously file a public prosecution. In the Da Zhonghua case, the families of the victims and the injured have already filed a private prosecution with the First Special District Court after the incident. The First Special District Court has also held several hearings on the case. Due to the provisions of the procedural law, the Shanghai Municipal Council cannot file a public prosecution. However, it can provide all available evidence to the families of the victims and the court for reference. Furthermore, the Shanghai Municipal Council does not intend to issue any formal statement before the case is concluded.

Rickshaw Owners Petition on Behalf of Rickshaw Pullers Against Compulsory Registration: Unsatisfactory Outcome 106

The French Concession Police Department's plan to implement compulsory registration for public rickshaw pullers from August 1 has caused unanimous opposition from rickshaw owners and pullers. The Shanghai Rickshaw Industry Association sent representatives Zhang Chuanyang, Qian Yuanjin, and Song Yaokun, with a petition, to the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce to request representative Yuan Hongjun to petition the Police Department. The head of the department, Guan Xuan, and the head of the station, Bo Ze, personally received the representatives, indicating that it was inconvenient to negotiate the rickshaw owners' request to suspend registration for now. If the rickshaw owners approve the registration, other issues cannot be accommodated. The representatives argued that although the 7,100 rickshaw licenses were donated by 195 people, there were over a thousand rickshaw owners, and even if the owners agree, each rickshaw puller has freedom, so they could not act on their behalf. Moreover, the association's petition was based on the resolution passed by the general assembly, and they could not change the proposal casually. Therefore, the outcome of the negotiations was not satisfactory. According to observers, if both parties hold extreme positions without a compromise, disputes will inevitably arise. The original petition from the Rickshaw Industry Association is transcribed below: "We, the Rickshaw Industry Association, respectfully submit this petition regarding the French Concession's public rickshaw puller registration. We have received instructions from your department to complete the registration within a specified period and have posted the processing methods. According to reports from rickshaw owners, although the owners have repeatedly advised the rickshaw pullers to comply with the regulations and register, the pullers' previous experiences of the police arbitrarily seizing permits and imposing heavy fines have made them fear the police department. Therefore, even if this registration is out of the good intentions and policies of the authorities, the rickshaw pullers find it difficult to trust. Moreover, the rickshaw pullers work hard all day, with calloused hands and feet, barely able to feed themselves, and the registration fees are too burdensome. Therefore, they unanimously refuse to register, declaring that they would rather be beggars and starve to death than register. Their attitude is firm, leaving the rickshaw owners with no options. If the owners force them, the pullers will inevitably abandon their rickshaws, which would greatly harm the rickshaw owners' business and impact municipal traffic. The public is worried. Please request the French Concession Police Department to consider the difficulties of the rickshaw industry and revoke the order. Your department's registration of rickshaw pullers only allows rickshaw owners to advertise and advise rickshaw pullers, and the right to register remains with the rickshaw pullers. Since the rickshaw pullers have unanimously expressed their opposition, it is necessary to carefully consider and re-evaluate the situation. We have heard that your department plans to ban unregistered vehicles from operating and force rickshaw pullers to register. If this is implemented, it will cause external disputes and greatly harm the rickshaw owners' business, which is not a good phenomenon for municipal traffic. Therefore, we have sent three committee members, Zhang Huaiyang, Yu Dakin, and Song Yaokun, to pay our respects and present the matter in person. We hope that you will grant us an audience and consider the difficulties of the rickshaw owners, revoking the order to register rickshaw pullers."

Case of China Industrial Bank: Court Notifies Settlement Plan, Creditors' Meeting Scheduled for This Afternoon to Discuss and Resolve Lu Xihou's Settlement Plan 113

The China Industrial Bank has been in liquidation since its collapse on October 11th of last year, and the court has yet to make a decision. The court-appointed accountant, Xu Yongzuo, is in charge of the liquidation. It is now known that the First Special District Court issued a notice and a settlement plan yesterday. A meeting of creditors is scheduled for 1:00 PM today at the Municipal Chamber of Commerce to discuss and resolve the matter. The court's notice and settlement plan are detailed below:

Court Notice: The First Special District Court of Jiangsu and Shanghai issued a notice yesterday, stating: "Regarding the case of Lu Xihou, Lu Mengxiang, et al., being declared bankrupt by the China Industrial Bank, a creditors' meeting is scheduled for 1:00 PM on July 31st of this year at the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce, located at the corner of North Henan Road and North Suzhou Road in Shanghai. Creditors are required to bring their debt registration certificate and creditors' meeting admission card to attend the meeting on time. If unable to attend in person, a representative may be appointed with a power of attorney. In addition to sending a summary of the settlement plan, this notice is hereby given. Included are a summary of the settlement plan, a ballot, and nine yes/no votes. This notice is issued to the creditors of the China Industrial Bank."

Settlement Plan: Lu Xihou, Lu Mengxiang, et al., the debtors of the China Industrial Bank who declared bankruptcy, proposed the following summary of the settlement plan: "The total amount of debt owed by the China Industrial Bank is now proposed to be settled at forty percent (i.e., forty yuan for every hundred yuan). Of this, twenty percent will first be paid off from the proceeds of the sale of all assets of the China Industrial Bank. If the proceeds are insufficient to cover the aforementioned twenty percent, the shortfall will be covered by Lu Xihou. In addition to the aforementioned twenty percent, for the remaining twenty percent to be paid, the debtors will separately sue the debtors of the China Industrial Bank to recover the debts. If the amount recovered exceeds twenty percent of the total liabilities of the China Industrial Bank, it will still be distributed to the creditors in proportion to the total amount of debt. If the amount recovered is less than twenty percent of the total liabilities, the shortfall will still be covered by Lu Xihou."

Aviation Lottery: Explanation of Drawing Procedures 114

The National Government Aviation Highway Construction Lottery has been issued for twelve periods. In order to improve the process, the office submitted a request to the Executive Yuan to change the drawing to once a month starting from the thirteenth period, and to reduce the number of tickets to 300,000. The number of winning tickets has been increased compared to the past, which is likely to attract the interest of ticket buyers. Sales for this period have been brisk, as already reported in various newspapers. As the drawing for the thirteenth period is approaching (August 9th), this reporter visited the office to inquire. According to the person in charge, in order to make the drawing procedures clear to ticket buyers, they are planning to print an explanation of the drawing process, so that people can fully understand it. The detailed drawing method and accompanying diagrams are detailed below for the benefit of readers.

Copper Drawing Machines: The drawing uses three copper machines (A, B, and C), mounted on iron stands. The machines are surrounded by semi-circular steel frames, allowing them to rotate freely. The interior of each machine is equipped with copper gears and wooden agitators. When the machine rotates, it agitates the small balls stored inside, evenly distributing them as they pass through the copper gears. Both the top and bottom of each machine are equipped with butterfly-shaped spring gates, releasing one small ball at a time, which rolls along a copper groove into a glass container.

Two Types of Balls: The small balls are divided into two types: ticket number balls and prize level balls, all made of pomelo wood. (1) The ticket number balls are placed in machines A and B. Machine A is larger, containing 3,000 ticket number balls, numbered from "0000" to "2999," representing the first four digits of the ticket number. Machine B is smaller, containing 100 ticket number balls, numbered from "00" to "99," representing the last two digits of the ticket number. (2) The prize level balls are placed in machine C, totaling 125. Among them, one is engraved with "1," four with "2," twenty with "3," and one hundred with "4." For example, if the prize level ball drawn is "1," it is the first prize. If "4" is drawn, it is the fourth prize. For the fifth prize (300 winners) and the sixth prize (600 winners), after the 125 prize level balls have been drawn, 1,000 ticket number balls, numbered from "000" to "999," are prepared separately, injected into machine C, mixed evenly, and three balls are drawn in sequence. All tickets whose last three digits match the three digits on the first ball drawn win the fifth prize. Tickets whose last three digits match the three digits on the second or third ball drawn win the sixth prize. For example, if the first ball is "213," the second ball is "465," and the third ball is "987," then all tickets whose last three digits are "213" win the fifth prize, and those whose last three digits are "465" or "987" win the sixth prize. All tickets whose last two digits match the last two digits of the first prize number win the seventh prize. Tickets whose last digit matches the last digit of the first prize number win the eighth prize, but those who have already won the seventh prize cannot also claim the eighth prize. The tickets with numbers immediately above and below the first prize number win the first prize consolation prize. For example, if the first prize number is "123456," then the numbers "123455" and "123457" win the first prize consolation prize. The tickets with numbers immediately above and below each of the second prize numbers win the second prize consolation prize. Since there are four second prize numbers, there are a total of eight second prize consolation prizes.

Drawing Order: During the drawing, supervisory committee members appointed by the National Government Aviation Highway Construction Lottery Committee, together with representatives from the local court, the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, and the Bankers' Association, will be present to supervise. First, the machines and balls used for the drawing are inspected in public. After the inspection, the balls are injected into the respective machines, and after multiple agitations, the drawing begins. All three machines simultaneously release one small ball, which rolls into the glass container at the end of each groove. The announcers standing beside the machines take out the balls under their charge and announce them in order. First, announcer A announces the four-digit number drawn from machine A. Next, announcer B announces the two-digit number drawn from machine B. Finally, announcer C announces the number on the ball drawn from machine C. The numbers on the two balls drawn from machines A and B are combined and read in order, which is the winning ticket number. The number on the ball drawn from machine C is the prize level won by that ticket. For example, if the number drawn from machine A is "1234," the number drawn from machine B is "56," and the number drawn from machine C is "1," then ticket number 123456 wins the first prize. If the number drawn from machine C is "4," then ticket number 123456 wins the fourth prize, and so on.

Strict Supervision: Each ticket number ball and prize level ball drawn is embedded on a ball board. In addition to reporting the numbers clearly under strict supervision, major prizes must be passed to the supervisory personnel for inspection, and the numbers on all three balls are photographed to emphasize their importance. The ticket number balls drawn from machines A and B are returned to their respective machines for continued drawing after verification, so that each ticket has an equal chance of winning. However, the prize level balls drawn from machine C are not returned. If the number of a small ball drawn from machines A and B has already won a prize, then any duplicate numbers drawn from the second time onwards will be considered invalid and immediately re-shuffled with the prize level balls drawn from machine C and re-drawn. A diagram is attached above.

Yangjiadu Fire Destroys Over 700 Houses: 5,000 Victims Urgently Need Relief, Scene of Devastation on All Sides, Two Fellow-Provincial Associations Meet to Discuss Relief Measures 115

At 8:30 PM the night before last, a fire broke out accidentally in the shantytown area south of Yangjiadu Beicaoni Pond in Pudong. The bamboo walls and thatched roofs were all highly flammable, causing the fire to spread rapidly. In addition, the southeasterly wind was exceptionally strong, adding fuel to the flames, which spread uncontrollably.

Although Director Zhao of the Shantou District Fire Brigade, Standing Committee Member Shen Yu of the Yangjing Town Fire Brigade, and other fire brigades from Laobaidu Tangqiao dispatched personnel to assist in the rescue efforts, they were unsuccessful. Hundreds of straw houses in the area were

Completely Destroyed within Three Hours. Details were reported in yesterday's newspaper. It is now known that Yang Zhongquan, the police chief of the Yangjiadu Police Station in charge of the area, ordered senior officers to investigate yesterday morning and estimated that approximately 700 straw sheds were destroyed or demolished, affecting approximately 500 households and

Over 5,000 Disaster Victims, including men, women, children, and the elderly. The severity of the disaster was greater than the previous fires. Furthermore, the Yangjing District Sixth Literacy School, located in Xichang Dongli in the area, was in session when the fire broke out. The students rushed home to salvage their belongings, and the teachers also hurriedly moved school equipment and books. Fortunately, the school building was saved by the firefighters' efforts, but

School Equipment and Books were Lost. The person responsible for the fire has been identified by the police station as Xu Zhengkai (also known as Xu), a native of Jiangbei. Xu had four straw sheds. Xu, his wife Wang, and his grandson lived in the two southern sheds, and his daughter-in-law lived in the two northern sheds. The cause of the fire is said to be that when catching bedbugs,

An Oil Lamp was Knocked Over, igniting the mosquito net. The police station dispatched officers to arrest Xu Zhengkai for questioning, but Xu had fled to avoid punishment. Only his wife, Wang, was taken to the station and transferred to the Public Security Bureau. Most of the victims of this disaster are homeless and are temporarily living in the

Vacant Land around the Fire Scene. The post-disaster situation is a scene of desolation, too terrible to witness. Police Chief Yang is planning to request assistance from various Shanghai charities to provide relief, as was done after previous disasters. Zhang Chiguang, Song Shixiang, Yan Hongxi, Shan Yuhua, Zhang Zhenshan, and others from the Taixian Fellow-Provincial Association, as well as

French Concession: Pawnshop Maturity Shortened to Twelve Months, Effective August 1st 117

The Shanghai Pawnbrokers Association stated that due to the sharp decline in prices, the 18-month maturity period for pawned goods has caused significant losses to members. They requested the Social Affairs Bureau to reduce the maturity period to 12 months, but this was not approved. The industry in the French Concession has announced that it will be changed to 12 months starting on August 1st. The original text reads: "Due to the economic downturn and the sharp drop in prices, women's clothing styles are constantly changing, and so are men's clothing styles. As a result, matured goods are outdated and no one cares about them. In order to maintain the pawnbroking industry, it is announced that starting from August 1st, the maturity period will be changed to twelve months. Upon maturity, customers who wish to retain their goods can extend the term at any time by adding interest. All goods pawned before this date will still be subject to the original regulations. This is hereby announced."

According to the International Trade Bureau yesterday, the bureau received letters requesting domestically produced products last week. These are published below, and exporting firms are requested to contact the bureau's guidance department for introductions. (1) "Dragon's Blood," a type of resinous substance (referring to rosin) that grows on rattan fruit, is produced in the Nanyang region, and is occasionally found in southern China. It is used to make lacquer and special tooth powders. Physicians use it as a medicine due to its calming and tonic properties. Surgeons can also use it to treat bleeding wounds. A British business office in this city is seeking this domestically produced product. (2) An American company, Bachu Company, needs various flower and tree seeds. (3) The Indian Gandhi Company needs henna leaves (balsam). (4) Niobium ore, often coexists with tungsten ore, and is occasionally produced in Jiangxi, Hunan, Guangdong, and Guangxi. Its main use is to make niobium steel. A certain company in this city needs this ore.

Two Deaths by Fire on Min Guo Road Yesterday 120

At 3:10 AM yesterday morning, a fire broke out at the New Xin Laundry Company at 679 Min Guo Road in the Chinese Concession, owned by Yan Zhihua, and on the third-floor attic of the landlord Yan Le at 683 Min Guo Road, due to carelessness. At that time, the wind was strong and the fire was very fierce, spreading to 679. Police officer Yu Pengjun of post No. 7 noticed the fire and immediately reported it to the Lao Bei Men Police Station, which then reported it to the fire brigade. A fire engine rushed to the scene and extinguished the fire, which took about an hour. Two buildings were destroyed, and an unknown man and a six-year-old girl named Ling Di were burned to death on the attic of 683. Afterwards, the police took Yan Zhihua, the owner of New Xin at 679, and Yan Le, the landlord at 683, to the station for questioning. According to Yan Zhihua's statement, "I live on the upper floor of 679 Min Guo Road. I don't know the cause of the fire. I have over 1,000 yuan of fire insurance. The dead man and girl are not from my family." According to Yan Le's statement, "I am the landlord at 683. The fire started in the attic on the third floor. The tenants are Lin A'san, an old woman, and a six-year-old girl, Ling Di. But the old woman is dead. Lin A'san has rented another house elsewhere. The dead girl is Ling Di, but I don't recognize the other man." Director Shen reviewed the statements and, as the case involved a fire and two deaths, ordered it to be sent to the bureau for strict handling.

British-American Tobacco Company Executive, Harris, Drills Well at Residence, Eruption of Flames, Fire Spreads Approximately Two to Three Zhang, Injuring Two Laborers, One of Whom Has Died 121

According to the Central News Agency, at 12:00 noon yesterday, a well-drilling project at the residence of Harris, the executive of the British-American Tobacco Company, located at 251 Yu Ni Gan Road (new address 284-286) on the western end of Da Xi Road in the western part of Shanghai, caused a eruption of flames, injuring two laborers. The Central News Agency reporter, considering this a novel incident, made a special visit to investigate.

A Glimpse of Harris' Residence: Yu Ni Gan Road, located on the western end of Da Xi Road, was built by the former Shanghai Municipal Council in the extraterritorial area. Although the trees planted on both sides have matured, the road surface is still earthen. Along the road, aside from a small Catholic church and the residence of Harris, the British-American Tobacco Company executive, all are farmland. Harris' residence is located on the north side of the road, covering approximately ten acres, surrounded by a short fence. A driveway winds to the house, which includes two new-style Western houses. The one in front is a two-story building, said to be occupied by Harris' daughter and son-in-law. The one in the rear is a three-story building, where Harris, approximately sixty years old, lives with his three sons. In addition, there are workshops, stables, and dog kennels, as well as a water tower. The remaining open space is maintained by a gardener, planting flowers and fruit, creating a pastoral atmosphere.

Well Drilling Causes Disaster: The fire-spewing well is located in the northwest corner of the residence, drilled to provide drinking water due to the inadequate water tower (there are no tap water pipes laid on this road). The well is approximately six to seven feet in diameter and five zhang deep, contracted to a foreign well-drilling company. With most of the work completed, the reporter found only three to five laborers resting, awaiting the foreman's orders. According to one of the laborers who witnessed the well explosion, the well walls are made of cement and steel reinforcement. Although spring water bubbled up from the bottom of the well, it was mixed with mud and unusable. Therefore, following the architect's instructions, several small holes were drilled in the well walls to allow water to seep into the well, preventing mud from forming. However, when laborers Wang Arong (age 18, from Shaoxing) and Li Zhifu (age 53, from Ningbo) entered the well and began working with axes, the contact of iron and stone generated sparks, which ignited a certain gas at the bottom of the well, causing an explosion. The sound was like thunder, heard by nearby farmers. Flames shot out of the well, reaching approximately two to three zhang into the sky. The thick hemp rope used for the windlass above the well was scorched, and the wood also showed signs of burning, illustrating the intensity of the fire at that moment.

Injured and Deceased Workers: Afterwards, the two laborers, Wang and Li, were rescued from the danger, their bodies charred black. They were immediately sent to Baolong Hospital on Buck Road for treatment. Wang Arong died from his injuries at 4:45 PM yesterday. Li Zhifu is still in critical condition and may not survive. The well owner, Harris, has ordered the work to be stopped, or perhaps the wellhead will be covered, as no one is willing to work in the well at any price.

Wu Palace Hotel: Man and Woman Attempt Suicide Together; Marriage Obstacles Lead to Suicide Attempt; Not Seriously Poisoned, Expected to Recover 122

At the Wu Palace establishment located at the intersection of Fuzhou Road and Fujian Road around 7 PM the night before last, a young man and woman suddenly arrived and checked in. The hotel's front desk clerk assigned them room number 412 on the fourth floor. The man identified himself as Zhang Rulin, 22 years old, a local resident, and the woman as Chen Chanjuan, 20 years old, from Nanxiang. The couple behaved normally that evening and went to sleep early. However, around 3 AM yesterday morning, the tea servers on that floor suddenly heard sounds of vomiting coming from the room. The tea servers, thinking the occupants were suffering from heatstroke, approached and knocked on the door. Receiving no response after a long wait, they grew suspicious and pushed the door open. They found the man and woman lying across the bed, faces pale and unconscious. Realizing something was wrong, they immediately reported to the front desk, who in turn notified the police station. The couple was transported by car to the hospital for treatment. Fortunately, the poisoning was not severe, and they are expected to recover. It was learned that the man, Zhang Rulin, is currently employed at Lanwei Advertising Printing Company and resides at No. 1 Yihe Lane, Fangxie Road, Nanshi. He and the woman, Chen Chanjuan, are deeply in love. However, due to family obstacles, their marriage faced difficulties. Out of resentment, they attempted suicide. The police station has notified their families to take them home.

Salvaging a Sunken Boat; Diver Suffocates; Blood Gushes from Mouth and Nose 125

Dai Chongli, a Ningbo fishing boat loaded with sand and gravel for sale in Shanghai, arrived at Dongpu Beach across from the Wusong Yunzaobang on the morning of the 27th of this month at 8 AM. The British Taikoo Company merchant ship "Haikou" was departing and, failing to avoid collision, struck the fishing boat amidships, causing it to sink immediately. Afterward, the sunken boat was moved by the tide and grounded near the Paotaiwan Customs Outpost (commonly known as "Huang Chuan"). The Zhanghuabang River Conservancy determined that the location was within a shipping lane used by vessels, and if the boat were not salvaged, it would obstruct the passage of ships. Consequently, the Junchupu Bureau Chief Engineer was commissioned to salvage the sunken boat. Yesterday afternoon, while the work was in progress, a diver named Yan Zhaolang, over 30 years old, from Jiangdong, Wusong, wearing a diving suit (i.e., a rubber suit), entered the water. He would work for about 50 minutes, then rest on the boat for 5 minutes before diving again. Less than 5 minutes into his second dive, the worker responsible for cranking the pump belt (which provided air) shouted because Zhaolang was not responding. The diving suit was pulled onto the deck, and the diver was found suffocated inside the rubber suit, with blood gushing from his mouth and nose. He was immediately transported to Wusong Health Hospital, but attempts to save him were unsuccessful, resulting in his tragic demise.

Zhabei Water and Electricity Company Changes Wusong Water Supply Fee Collection Method; Municipal Public Utilities Bureau Has Submitted to the Municipal Government for Approval 126

The water supply in Wusong and other areas of this city has been contracted to the Zhabei Water and Electricity Company since February of this year, with the approval of the Municipal Government. Water pipes have already been laid by the company to Wusong Town. Although the town is within the city limits, the residents are relatively poor. Therefore, a revised fee collection method has been proposed to encourage water connection and achieve the goal of providing clean drinking water. The regulations stipulate that residents in the Wusong area who install 13mm and 20mm water meters will be exempt from paying the deposit. The monthly rental fee for a 13mm water meter is 20 cents (silver dollar), and for a 20mm water meter, it is 30 cents (silver dollar). Regardless of the number of houses, the water fee deposit is uniformly four dollars per household. For water meters of 25mm or larger, the regulations of the Water Sales Business Charter will still be followed. Connection fees will be calculated based on the actual cost of labor and materials according to the size of the water meter installed. If the calculated cost of labor and materials exceeds the amount stipulated in the regulations, the actual cost of labor and materials will be charged to ensure accuracy. This method has been submitted by the company to the Municipal Public Utilities Bureau for approval by the Municipal Government for a two-year trial period to promote water usage.
