Traditional Chinese Medicine Doctor Zhu Shuping Accused of Negligence; Two-Year-Old Child Dies, Causing Dispute; Case Concluded and Judgment Today 128

Zhu Shuping, a traditional Chinese medicine pediatrician from County Kettle at No. 500 Changsha Road, treated the two-year-old child of Sun Hu's family last month. After diagnosis, he determined that the child was suffering from lingering illness after measles with dangerous symptoms. After prescribing medication, the child did not respond to the treatment and died shortly after. Sun Hu's family claimed that the death of her child was caused by the Ephedra and Aconite prescribed by Zhu, and filed a criminal complaint against Zhu Shuping for negligence. Zhu denied that the prescribed medication had any impropriety and filed a counterclaim against Sun Hu's family for false accusation. The First Special District Court summoned the parties and, with the consent of both parties, sent the prescription to the Traditional Chinese Medicine Association for expert evaluation, as previously reported. Yesterday afternoon was the date for the continued hearing of the case. Judge Liu Yugui first distributed the evaluation report from the Traditional Chinese Medicine Association to the lawyers for both parties for review. The lawyer for the plaintiff, Shen Yong, stated that he could not trust the evaluation report because the Traditional Chinese Medicine Association was a professional organization, and requested that the prescription be re-evaluated by an academic organization to ensure fairness. The defendant's defense lawyer, Zhang Enhao, objected, stating that the previous decision to have the Traditional Chinese Medicine Association perform the evaluation was agreed upon by both parties, so why change the decision now? Furthermore, Shen was already a member of the Traditional Chinese Medicine Association and its legal advisor, and should not have contempt for or distrust the official organization and the report it had produced after deliberation. At that time, lawyer Shen presented a medical book, stating that it could prove the defendant's improper use of medicine. The court then questioned the defendant, Zhu Shuping, who stated that both Ephedra and Aconite were effective in opening the lungs and treating lingering illness after measles, and that the other medicines either helped to resolve phlegm or had the effect of strengthening the foundation. In short, all the medicines in the prescription were related, and treatment should not rely entirely on medical books. Furthermore, the child's illness was very severe, and he had told the people holding the child and so on. Next, the plaintiff, Sun Hu's family, stated that the child's illness was quite mild that day, so they only asked the wet nurse to take the child. If the illness had been serious, even if they did not invite a doctor to the house, they would have taken the child themselves. However, the child died that night after taking the medicine, so they were certain that the death was due to the wrong medication. At the end, after mutual debate between the lawyers for the two parties, Judge Liu ordered the parties to wait for the pronouncement (today) in the afternoon.

He did not know about the current kidnapping case. Both of them claimed that they were having tea at the Laohuzao when they were mistakenly arrested. The third was Lu Miaolin, also from Tongzhou, living at No. 28, Lianhua Lane, Lujiabang. He stated that he and Lu Liangguang were cousins, but they did not interact, so he did not know what they were doing. He did not expect that when they caught him, they would bring him here. After reviewing the statements, the questioner considered the case to be significant and requiring further investigation.

Medical Overview of the Emergency Epidemic Hospital 138

The Emergency Epidemic Hospital at the intersection of North Xizang Road and Kaifeng Road opened on the 7th of this month. As of yesterday, the epidemic department had 767 outpatient visits. Among them, five people died shortly after arriving at the hospital because they could not be treated in time. The cause of death was unknown for three people, heatstroke for too long for one person, and a diabetic coma diagnosed by urine test for one person. In the 20 days of hospital admission, a total of 163 people were admitted, of whom 8 died. The causes of death are as follows: (1) Malignant gastroenteritis (i.e., pseudo-cholera) 1 person, (2) Dysentery 1 person, (3) Central pneumonia, (4) Typhoid fever 2 people (one with intestinal bleeding), (5) Enteritis 2 people (one with pneumonia and the other with heart disease), (6) Heatstroke 1 person. The hospital has its own laboratory, so the diagnosis is easier to understand. The outpatient department is staffed by well-known experts in Shanghai's medical community, who provide free diagnosis and treatment for various departments, including pediatrics, gynecology, and venereology, which have already reached more than 2,000 patients.

Four Banks Joint Savings Society Issues Reserve Report; Two Hundred and Ninetieth First Time 139

The Four Banks Joint Savings Society was jointly established by the Yanye, Jincheng, Zhongnan, and Dalu banks to handle the issuance of Zhongnan Bank banknotes. According to the society's issuance charter, banknotes are issued with full reserves. Cash reserves must be at least 60% and guaranteed reserves must be at most 40%. It is announced once a week and audited by the auditors and accountants of the four banks. Now, the Two Hundred and Ninetieth First announcement of the Shanghai Reserve Bank on July 27, 1935, is recorded below: Banknote circulation amount: 19,344,473 yuan. Total amount of reserves: 19,344,473 yuan. Includes: Cash reserves: 16,662,993 yuan, Guaranteed reserves: 2,681,480 yuan.

Another Woman Sues Ruan Kaiji for Illegal Detention and Obstruction of Freedom 143

Ruan Kaiji, the former chief of the Xinzha Branch of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, who had already been suspended from his position, along with bureau members Zheng Zuhan and others, jointly filed a lawsuit in the local court accusing him of dereliction of duty, etc. The court held several trials, and the result was that the accusations made by Zheng and others lacked sufficient evidence, and a decision was made not to prosecute. Unexpectedly, recently, another woman, Tu Xu Shi, sued Ruan Kaiji in the local court for illegal arrest and abuse of power, as well as Jiang Weiyu for false accusation. The details of the case and the court hearing are recorded below. It is said that a local man named Tu Axiang, who lives at No. 1446 Qiujiang Road, Zhabei, is a standing director of the municipal cattle slaughtering industry union. At the end of last month, a small number of workers in Jiang Weiyu's Jiangxiangxing cattle slaughtering workshop went on strike. When the Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs was mediating impartially, Jiang Weiyu believed that the striking workers were instigated by Tu Axiang, so he reported to the Xinzha Branch and sent police to summon Tu Axiang without success. Therefore, Tu's wife, Tu Xu Shi, was detained at the bureau. The next day, she was sent to the Public Security Bureau and released. Three of the striking workers were detained by the branch and sent to the local court. After the prosecutor's interrogation, they were also given a decision not to prosecute. Now, Tu Xu Shi has hired lawyer Lu Qi to file a direct complaint with the criminal court of the local court, accusing Jiang Weiyu of false accusation and colluding with Ruan Kaiji, the chief of the Xinzha Branch, to illegally detain her and obstruct her freedom, requesting a thorough investigation. After the court received the complaint, Judge Tan Zhuohong specially opened the tenth court at 10:00 AM yesterday to hear the case. The plaintiff, Tu Xu Shi, and her lawyer Lu Qi arrived in court successively. The defendants, Jiang Weiyu and Ruan Kaiji, also hired lawyers Fan Gang and Zhang Fukang to appear in court and defend them. First, Tu Xu Shi testified that she was 31 years old, from Qingpu. On the first day of this month, at about 4:00 PM, Jiang Weiyu led the police to her house and asked if her husband, Tu Axiang, was at home. She replied that her husband had left for Suzhou a few days ago due to some business. Jiang and others did not believe her and went into the bedroom to search. Because there was no trace of her husband, Jiang and others ordered her to go to the police station with them. She said that she had many children at home and no one to take care of them for the time being, and even if she went, the police station would have to make arrangements in advance. Unexpectedly, Jiang and others ignored the situation and slapped her repeatedly, handcuffed her with Western-style handcuffs, and dragged her to the police station for detention. When she said this, she could not help but shed tears. The judge ordered the defendant Jiang Weiyu to the stand, who stated that he was 27 years old, a local, and lived at No. 687 Jiaotong Road. The judge asked her how she would defend herself against the charge of obstructing freedom. Jiang replied that after the strike occurred in his shop on July 1, the striking workers said that it was Tu Axiang who instigated them. He immediately reported to the police station, and the police station ordered him to point out Tu Axiang and bring two policemen with him. The judge asked why Tu Xu Shi was detained. Jiang replied that he did not know, but at that time, Tu Axiang was out, and she voluntarily went to the police station. Tu Xu Shi said sternly that they used coercive means to arrest her. She was eating dinner, and they beat her and searched her husband in her house. She told them that her husband had gone to Suzhou. She went to the room to change her shoes, and they said she was going to escape. They kicked her and beat her, and because she refused to go, they handcuffed her. Lawyer Lu Qi stated that Ruan Kaiji had not arrived today. Did the court's summons receive? The judge then turned to lawyer Fan Gang and said that Ruan Kaiji must comply with the summons and appear in court next time. Lawyer Fan agreed. Lawyer Lu Qi added that the Central Government, the Central Party Department, the Control Yuan, the Municipal Government, and other agencies were paying attention to this case and thoroughly investigating it. The judge then adjourned the court for further joint trial.

Correction: In our newspaper on the 20th of this month, there was a report about an Indian man raping a Chinese maid. According to the investigation, this report is inaccurate, because the Indian man and the Chinese woman did not violate any criminal law.

The Xujiahui Observatory's weather forecast at 4:30 PM yesterday stated that Shandong's surroundings are cloudy and foggy, the wind direction is calm, and there is dust. The Yangtze River basin is cloudy with light showers and moderate to strong southeast to northeast winds. The East China Sea is cloudy with strong southeast winds. Great World: Verdict in the Attempted Murder of Wife Case; Zhao Jishan Sentenced to Five Years in Prison 145

Zhao Jishan, a native of Zhenjiang, who lives at No. 71 Xinkangli, Kangnuo Road, and is a Chinese medicine practitioner at Guangyi Hospital on Roberts Road, is 32 years old this year. He married Leng (34 years old this year), a woman from the same village, seven years ago. Because she did not bear any children, Zhao also took his sister-in-law's younger sister, Zhong Zhendi (25 years old this year), as a concubine. They lived together for five years and had a daughter. Because the wife and concubine lived together, they often quarreled, causing Leng to be intolerable to the concubine. Zhao, harboring evil intentions, on the afternoon of the 4th of this month, ostensibly took his wife, Leng, to the Great World for entertainment. At 7:30 PM, Zhao lured Leng to the fifth floor of the amusement park, along the roof platform facing the Edward Road side near the dance stage, and pretended to say to Leng, "Let's hug each other to test each other's weight." First, Leng lifted Zhao up. After putting him down, Zhao lifted Leng up and threw her over the railing, trying to kill her. Fortunately, Leng grabbed the railing in fright and shouted for help. A waiter named Zhu Jinfu rushed to rescue her and sent her and Zhao to the cashier, who handed them over to the patrolman and sent them to the French Concession Police Station. Investigator Ma Yizhi was dispatched to investigate and escorted Zhao to the Special No. 2 Court. The police legal advisor filed a public prosecution according to Article 276 of the new criminal law for attempted murder. Judge Li Changnian held several hearings to investigate the details, which have been recorded in this newspaper. The trial of this case has now concluded. At the beginning of the verdict yesterday, at 9:00 AM, Judge Li came to the first criminal court and ordered the defendant Zhao Jishan to be brought to the stand. After briefly questioning his age and origin, he announced the verdict: Zhao Jishan was sentenced to five years of imprisonment for attempted murder. The number of days of detention before the judgment is finalized will be counted as one day of imprisonment. During the appeal period, he was ordered to be transferred to the detention center for further instructions. It is said that the defendant expressed dissatisfaction with the verdict and intended to appeal.

Education News

Guangzhou Municipal Middle Schools to Implement Coeducation Separation 146

To be Implemented Starting This Academic Year

Designated Municipal No. 2 Middle School to Enroll All Female Students

Guangzhou Municipal Elementary and Secondary Schools have always been coeducational. Recently, in order to improve the efficiency of education and enable male and female students to concentrate on their studies, the Municipal Bureau of Education proposed that municipal middle schools separate male and female students for instruction. This was discussed at the 158th Municipal Administrative Meeting and immediately resolved to implement coeducation separation, with the names remaining the same. Municipal No. 1 Middle School and No. 3 Middle School were designated to enroll only male students, and Municipal No. 2 Middle School was designated to enroll only female students. No. 1 and No. 2 Middle Schools each reduced one senior and junior high school class, while No. 3 Middle School increased two senior and junior high school classes. Teachers' salaries and benefits were standardized, with senior high school teachers receiving eight yuan per hour and junior high school teachers receiving six yuan. The budgets of each school were based on the principle of not exceeding the total budget for this year. The implementation was scheduled to begin in the autumn of this year (the 24th year of the Republic). According to recent investigations, after the case was passed, municipal middle schools have begun preparations, and the number of classes in each school has changed. The reason is that the Second Middle School has a total of 13 classes of male and female students, and now it completely accepts 11 classes of female students. The First Municipal Middle School originally had 20 classes of male and female students, but now it has reduced two classes to 18 classes. The Third Municipal Middle School originally had 4 classes of male and female students, and now it has increased four classes to 8 classes. Although the number of classes in the three schools may increase or decrease this time, they actually offset each other, but the original budgets of each school need to be slightly modified, but there is no increase in municipal expenditure.

As for municipal elementary schools, they are still coeducational. The Municipal Bureau of Education recently received a subsidy of 50,000 yuan from the central government, which will be used to expand short-term compulsory elementary schools starting this year in order to accommodate out-of-school children in the city. Private schools in the city are still strictly prohibited, and those with good results will be subsidized according to their grades, while those that have not improved will be ordered to disband. In addition, the Bureau of Education recently selected one or two elementary schools in the city to test the new four-year system. It is reported that the results are quite good, and it will be designed to promote this four-year elementary school system in the autumn. (July 28)

Children's Year Opening Ceremony to Be Held at the Municipal Government Tomorrow 147

Children Participating Will Be Picked Up and Dropped Off by Cars Provided by the Association Mayor and Others to Review Various Child Welfare Organizations in the Afternoon Public Places and Hospitals Open for Free Examinations Airplane Performances, Radio Broadcasts, and Entertainment

Since the central government stipulated that this year from August 1 to July 31 next year will be the National Children's Year, the Municipal Government ordered the Municipal Social Education, Health, and Public Security Bureaus to organize a Children's Year Implementation Committee. The committee, with the opening date approaching, re-appointed committee members to be responsible for preparing for the opening ceremony. The preparatory committee held its last meeting the day before yesterday and invited school representatives and entertainers in the evening. The entire program for the opening day has been decided. The details are as follows:

Opening Ceremony

At 9:00 AM on August 1, 1,000 children representatives from various schools, factories, and child welfare organizations will hold the opening ceremony in the Municipal Government Auditorium. The order is as follows: (1) Play music and open the meeting, (2) Sing the party song, (3) Bow three times to the national flag, the party flag, and the portrait of the Prime Minister, (4) The chairman respectfully reads the Prime Minister's will, (5) The chairman delivers the opening address, (6) Speeches, (7) Children representatives deliver speeches, (8) Sing the Children's Year song, (9) Play music and dismiss the meeting. When children attending the big meeting arrive at the Municipal Government by car, the association will pay the car fare after each school hires its own car.

Meeting Staff

The opening ceremony will be chaired by Mayor Wu Tiecheng, Director of the Social Affairs Bureau Wu Xingya, Director of the Education Bureau Pan Gongzhan, Director of the Health Bureau Li Ting'an, Director of the Public Security Bureau Cai Jingjun, and representatives from the Municipal Party Department. Wang Xianqing will be the master of ceremonies, and the Children's Year Implementation Committee members Zhang Binghui, Jiang Jianbai, Chen Bai, Lin Yannan, Sun Yongyi, Chen Lengyi, Rao Qiangsheng, Wang Gang, Xu Gongmei, Hu Shuyi, Zhou Shang, Hu Changzhi, Zhou Guobao, Yin Guanzhi, Yuan Liangzou, Chen Tiesheng, Wang Zhenchang, Wang Yisun, Zhang Zixin, Qian Fugong, Zhou Wanghe, etc. will take care of everything separately. Wang Zhenchang is designated as the chief receptionist, Guo Junshi manages the car fare for children attending, Yan Wenkai manages the gifts for children, Yuan Zengyu is responsible for radio broadcasting, Xu Gongmei is responsible for entertainment, and Wang Gang is responsible for preparing vehicles to send children back to Shanghai.

Receiving Representatives

After the completion of the opening ceremony, the mayor and the director of the Social Affairs Bureau will receive children representatives in the mayor's reception room, inquire about the children's living conditions, and give instructions and encouragement.

Airplane Performance

The Children's Air Force plane donated by the children of this city to the Central Government will fly to Shanghai together with two other planes donated by this city, and will perform a flight display in the square in front of the Municipal Government at 10:30 AM to arouse children's interest in aviation.

Reviewing Organizations

Starting at 2:00 PM, the mayor, directors, and representatives from various agencies will review the city's child welfare organizations, such as the Vagrant Vocational Training Center, Children's Department, Orphanage, Civilian Education Center, Women and Children Relief Association, Jiangwan Asylum, Child Welfare Education Center, Zhabei Huier Orphanage, etc., and will be reviewed and instructed by the officials.

On August 1, all major newspapers in the city will open a special section to publish the Children's Year opening supplement. The mayor, directors, and experts who are enthusiastic about children's affairs all have papers, which are being compiled and distributed by the preparatory committee.

Gifts and Souvenirs

All children participating in the opening ceremony and review will be given a commemorative badge by the mayor. Notices for Private Schools in the Public Concession to Receive Subsidies 153

In order to promote education, the Public Concession Bureau allocates a certain amount of funds every year as subsidies for private Chinese and Western schools within the concession. All private Chinese schools within the concession whose management equipment and teaching performance are deemed satisfactory by the bureau and who truly need financial assistance can apply to the bureau for this subsidy. The method of receiving the subsidy is as follows: all schools that have been registered with the Municipal Education Bureau should first apply to the Municipal Education Bureau, and the bureau will issue application forms and regulations printed by the Public Concession Bureau. Then, the principals of each school should fill in the forms, affix their seals, and submit them to the Municipal Education Bureau. After the examination is qualified, the Municipal Education Bureau will transfer them to the Public Concession Bureau for verification and decision. Those who have not been registered with the Municipal Education Bureau can directly apply to the Education Department of the Public Concession Bureau, and the department will issue application forms and regulations, etc., which should be completed truthfully in accordance with the regulations and submitted to the department for review and processing. In addition, Western schools within the concession and special donation areas can also apply to the Education Department of the Public Concession Bureau for this subsidy. The method is the same as that for Chinese schools that have not been registered with the Municipal Education Bureau. However, all forms and petitions for the subsidy for 1936 should be submitted to the Education Department no later than October 1 of this year.

Fujian Province's Plans for Physical Education and Reflections on Returning from a Southern Tour Wu Yunrui, Wu Cheng, Cheng Dengke

Zheng Xinnan, Director of the Education Department of Fujian Province, is a famous contemporary scientist. Since taking charge of education in Fujian Province, his achievements have been remarkable. Mr. Zheng has a grand vision of saving the country through science, so in recent years he has spent 50,000 to 60,000 yuan to establish an extremely well-equipped science museum in the center of the provincial capital, so that public and private primary schools in the provincial capital can use it nearby without having to prepare their own scientific instruments. The savings in expenses are self-evident. The classrooms, student laboratories, and specialized research rooms are all fully equipped. Recently, the scientific equipment in the provincial capital has been extended to the entire province, and it has been clearly stipulated that the last year was Science Year, supplementing the expenses of each school to set up scientific instruments. In the past year, it has already taken shape. Director Zheng also sees the weakness of the people of Fujian Province and the importance of national physical education, so in addition to scientific equipment, physical education equipment should be expanded to build a foundation for promoting school physical education. Therefore, he resolutely designated the 24th year as Physical Education Year, hired Wu Demao, a lecturer in the Physical Education Department of Central University, as a consultant to the provincial government and a physical education supervisor, and together with Tang Yichong, the third section chief, held summer workshops for primary and secondary schools, with a physical education group set up inside, ordering primary and secondary school teachers and social education institutions to send personnel to attend lectures, and inviting Fang Wanbang, a physical educationist from the province, to return to Fujian to lecture. Because Fang could not stay in Fujian for the entire period, he invited colleagues to assist him. This is the reason for the colleagues' trip to Fujian.

The physical education group had 96 male and female students. All the subjects were quite practical. Taking advantage of the colleagues' presence in Fujian, Director Zheng also gathered the principals of secondary schools throughout the province to hold a physical education discussion meeting. In order to promote the advancement of physical education throughout the province, he gathered the principals of public and private schools throughout the province in one hall and held a specialized meeting. This is truly a pioneering effort for physical education colleagues to join hands with middle school principals. At this meeting, it was stipulated that 1% to 3% of the total school expenses should be used for physical education expenses. The sports fees paid by students must be kept independent and not be misappropriated. The principal must submit it to the Education Department for approval before it can be used. In this physical education year, each school must have the minimum physical education equipment ready, and the physical education supervisor will inspect and assess them and give praise or criticism. Director Zheng also deeply knows that to promote physical education, the education of talent must be given priority, so it was decided to open a physical education normal class at Fuzhou Normal School starting in the 24th year, in order to train leading talent and make a foundation for promoting physical education throughout the province. The establishment of a physical education department in a provincial normal school is unprecedented except for Hebei Province. The above are all good results of this meeting.

In addition to the 7th Division, the Fuzhou garrison also has a military police regiment. Soldiers are often seen doing freehand exercises on the sports field and playing ball games, adding a lot of color to the sports field. Ji Zhangjian, the head of the military police regiment, has achieved excellent results in Fujian and is deeply loved by the people, and he is very supportive of physical education. He often personally takes the lead as a model for the soldiers, ordering physical education instructor Wu Zibin to hold various ball game round-robin competitions and regimental sports meets in each team under the regiment's jurisdiction. According to Regiment Head Ji, a large-scale military and police sports meet will be held soon to promote physical education.

Hot springs are a specialty of Fuzhou, and bathhouses are everywhere. The attention to detail can be said to be the best in the country. It is also heard that the provincial capital plans to set up a large-scale hot spring swimming pool jointly run by the government and businesses to cultivate the people's ability to engage in water activities. The design drawings for this swimming pool have already been drawn by engineers and will be started as soon as funding is available.

Director Zheng not only pays attention to school physical education but also to social physical education. In this physical education year, he will also promote it at the same time, ordering each county to improve the existing sports fields and add new sports fields if they do not have them. Whether it is in politics, academics, or work, if there are certain steps and annual plans, nothing will not be successful. After a two-week tour of Fujian, the colleagues had this very good impression and were deeply pleased for the future of physical education in Fujian Province. The following is a general summary of the thoughts on the tour of Fujian:

(1) The physical education community will be united from now on. Lin Yin'nan, a physical education instructor in Fujian Province, is a veteran of the physical education community. Fujian's physical education has what it has today thanks to Lin's efforts. Now knowing the importance of the tasks in the Physical Education Year, it is definitely not something that the strength of a few people can do, so he takes a leading position and advocates a grand alliance of the physical education community, eliminating personal prejudices and academic factional disputes, and jointly planning the advancement of physical education in Fujian Province to achieve the heavenly duty of revitalizing the nation. His correctness of vision is admired by the colleagues. From now on, the progress of physical education in Fujian Province will be due to Lin's call to awaken the confused dream.

(2) The students' focus on research in Fujian Province for several weeks, just in time for the hot summer, and each student has five hours of academic subjects every morning and two or three hours of technical subjects in the afternoon. Sometimes there are discussion meetings at night, and each student is eager to learn, asking questions when they have doubts. This scale of eagerness to learn is truly admirable. The colleagues are ashamed of their shallow learning, and in this situation, they cannot help but try to make it difficult. Pursuing memories along the way still has some joy. (To be continued)

Snippets 163

— (Xu Jiawu)

Time passes by in a clickety-clack manner, and people advance like oxen in the process of conquering nature.

Space-time is the warp and weft of the universe; however, without people, who use different perceptions and energies in different environments to think and create, how could space-time, however great, weave into a pattern of different colors that hangs forever?

"An inch of time is an inch of gold, but an inch of gold cannot buy an inch of time." Clever and skillful socializers, after eating their fill, interpret the saying literally, holding a fiftieth-plus-one birthday celebration today, and a sixtieth birthday celebration tomorrow, as if the continuation of life and the accumulation of time are something worth boasting about and rejoicing in!

"Young in age, inexperienced in the world"; "Hair already white, why not die sooner?" Originally ephemeral beings in space-time, how many ambitions and achievements are lost in this traditional, passive view of age!

Mr. Chun 164

— Wu Yafei

Mr. Chun was a scholar who passed the imperial examination in the Qing Dynasty. Not long ago, he was admired by many people, but now he has retired to the countryside, making a living as a doctor. He no longer advises on any current affairs, as if he wants to escape from the world and leisurely spend his old age.

Recently, he has become somewhat disgusted with the world, because the world has given him a bad impression; therefore, he feels somewhat sad about everything now. However, what makes him most angry is the behavior of his son and daughter, which is completely out of line.

"Oh! I was too foolish, I regret sending them to those foreign schools; now they have become neither male nor female, what are they like! Young girls can go out all day long to flirt with boyfriends, and young men don't want to work all day long, but take women to the cinema and dance hall to talk about love; it's a disgrace, alas! This world..." Thinking of this, he almost burst into flames: "It's absurd that a father can't control his children!"

Indeed, Mr. Chun is a descendant of a family of scholars, how can he compare himself with ordinary families without thresholds? Now his son and daughter dare to disobey his family education and go out to socialize like crazy, isn't this deliberately messing with him? It really made his yellow beard stand up in anger.

"Ah! It's rebellious, it's rebellious, the world has been brought to this point, men and women are indistinguishable, how can it be! And even the father can't control the children anymore. What's with not even saying hello to the father when they see him, and asking for money as soon as they meet, and clamoring for a family revolution if they don't get it; okay, from tomorrow on, they won't be allowed to enter the house, and I'll publish a notice disowning them." He paced around the study in circles, muttering to himself, and when he said he would publish a notice disowning them, he hit the table with his fist, as if it added a lot of courage to him.

Feeling a little tired, he sat down on a rocking chair by the window, picked up a small teapot, and took a sip of ginseng tea, as if it calmed the anger in his chest.

Although he just said that he would publish a notice disowning them, now that he thought about it calmly, it wasn't right. This would not only make relatives and friends laugh; moreover, my Qin family only has that one line of descent, "There are three forms of unfilial piety, the worst is to have no descendants," no, I should still teach them well! Thinking like this, all anger subsided.

Conservative 165

— Wan

If only Englishmen are the most conservative people in the world, then Mr. Ji Mu is the epitome of an Englishman. He is a playboy, but he is different from other playboys, he is an old playboy who is almost sixty years old, his different places are: ordinary playboys, mostly like the new and hate the old, ambitious, he is not; he does not dislike the old, especially does not like the new, more afraid of people talking about ambitious problems; he is suspicious of, curses, criticizes, and ridicules all new things, unless they are newly minted silver coins, newly printed banknotes, he cannot not use them. The house he lives in is in a very old alley, and the insurance period of the house has exceeded ten years ago. Because he wants to preserve his vitality, he not only does not take a bath all year round, but even his feet are rarely washed once or twice, he refuses to cut his nails when they grow long, his teeth are loose, and he even refuses to ask a dentist to pull them out, saying that he wants to preserve the remains of his parents, he eats Fujian Golden Lion brand skin silk cigarettes, and has not changed the brand for thirty years, he also smokes Old Beauty cigars, also thirty years as one day, his bedroom corner is piled up with empty cigar boxes, reaching the ceiling, and he never wants to abandon them. On his table, there is a broken Shenbao newspaper from fifteen years ago as a cushion, he eats one bowl for lunch and two bowls for dinner every day, even if he is not full, or can't eat it, he never wants to add or subtract a mouthful. He has a monk's cap brand cigarette box from twenty-nine years ago on his cupboard, an old satin cap from forty years ago, a bamboo ear pick from ten years ago, and... years ago... In short, entering his house is like entering a museum of antiques.

御香縹緲錄 167

— Princess Der Ling, translated by Qin Shouou

Such compassionate actions, though not uncommon in our Chinese history, and among the monarchs of past dynasties, there was no lack of those who loved their people like children; but whether His Oldness created this idea himself, or whether he intentionally emulated the ancients, it can always be considered admirable.

Because I knew of such an incident, I firmly believe that she was a kind-hearted old lady, and she must have been mindful of the traitor's past merits and his family, and could not decisively determine the punishment he should receive.

When it comes to punishment, the most severe is naturally beheading or hanging! The next most severe is for the imperial court to issue an edict instructing him to commit suicide by taking medicine, or by slitting his throat, or by hanging himself. According to the current crimes of this Guangdong governor, beheading and hanging are certainly too cruel; a more appropriate punishment would be to order him to commit suicide. However, the Empress Dowager still felt unbearable in her heart, so should he just be let off? No; no, although the Empress Dowager was compassionate, she would not deliberately favor him and lose the meaning of impartiality; thus, the following memorial was issued by the Grand Council the next day. Within a few days, all of China knew about this matter.

"By imperial decree: The Guangdong Governor ×× is corrupt and perverts the law, and his reputation is tarnished. The former Minister of the Ministry of Revenue ×× and the Vice Minister of the Ministry of Justice ×× were sent to investigate. According to the report, the investigation is true, and he should be dismissed immediately and sent to Heilongjiang, never to be employed again; his property should also be seized by the Jiangsu Province (because the hometown of the offending governor is in Suzhou) Governor ×× and ordered by the local officials to be sealed and confiscated. Respect this."

This punishment seems to be very light, and all of this happened more than thirty years ago, but its impact has not diminished to this day. (378)

Chapter Seventeen: Do Not Ask a Daughter's Body Difficult to Say Hidden Pain Contend to See Noble Person's Face Commonly Admire Noble Demeanor

So on the surface, Zhang Jiefu would not help anymore, he was not responsible. World Rare News

世界最大的大胖子 170

— Hai Ke

The World's Biggest Fat Man 171

— Hai Ke

Robert Ruggendorf, Germany's only fat man, recently died in Rossburg. His body weighed 539 pounds, and he made a living by publicly displaying his fat figure. When he went on trips, he could only ride in freight trains, because the doors of passenger cars were too small to allow him to enter and exit, so he had a specially prepared motorcycle that could accommodate his mountain of flesh for long journeys. The front door of the house he lived in was specially enlarged, more than twice the size of his neighbors' doors, so one can imagine how fat he was.

However, Ruggendorf, although fat, was not as fat as the Englishman Edward Bright, who, at the time of his death, weighed 616 pounds, with a circumference of five feet six inches, a chest circumference of six feet eleven inches, and a mid-arm circumference of one foot six inches. He did not exhibit himself to people, but made a living by selling groceries, and eventually died at the age of thirty because his body became fatter and fatter every day. After he died, someone in Maldon bet that five men of twenty-one could be wrapped in his sleeve, but the result was that ten people could be wrapped in it, and the sleeve was still stiff. Bright was survived by a wife and five children. He was very cheerful in nature, and his appetite was not that much larger than that of ordinary people, but in the years before his death, he drank a gallon of beer every day. After his death, the coffin could not be carried out of the door, so the wall had to be opened before it could be carried out.

The two people above were fat, but there was also the world's biggest fat man, whose name was Daniel Lambert, who weighed 739 pounds a few days before his death, with a waist circumference of nine feet four inches, and a leg circumference of thirty-seven inches. Each time he had a suit made, the tailor charged a huge sum of twenty gold pounds. He was born in Leicester, England, and was as strong as an ox, easily lifting 600 pounds. Once, a large circus bear bullied a dog on the street, he took great offense and fought with the bear, eventually defeating it and letting the dog go. Lambert was also a very skilled swimmer in his youth, his large body floating high on the water, his back able to accommodate two strong men standing on it, as if standing on a raft.

Lambert's father was not fat, his figure was about average, he was a jailer in the Leicester prison. When he retired in his old age, Lambert continued to serve as a jailer. His heart was as big as his body, so he treated the prisoners with particular kindness, never mistreating them. Later, because of his diligent service, he rose step by step, eventually rising to the position of warden, and when he retired, the government gave him a generous pension. Only because he was too fat, wherever he went, many people would surround him to look at him, so after he retired, he had nothing to do, so he simply made a public exhibition of himself. Although he did not make a living from this, rather than being confined to his own home, why not go out and make money with his fat body? He lived in Piccadilly, where he was exhibited, his style was very grand, everything was very particular, and important figures of the time often went to see him, which made his value even higher. For several years, his exhibition business was very prosperous, and he earned a lot of money. Later, he died in the town of Stamford in Lincolnshire, but he still holds the highest record for the world's fattest man.

Bright died at the age of thirty, Lambert at the age of forty, and the recent Ruggendorf died at the age of forty-seven, so it can be seen that being fat is indeed a disease, and fat people often cannot enjoy old age.

Additional Special Margin Required for Cotton Yarn Delivery: 800 Yuan for Cotton Yarn, 300 Yuan for Raw Cotton 182

The Shanghai Cotton Yarn Exchange has announced that, starting from July 31st, a special cash margin of 800 yuan per 100 bales will be required for both buyers and sellers in new cotton yarn transactions for all months. For new raw cotton transactions for all months, a special cash margin of 300 yuan per 100 bundles will be required. A notice has been posted regarding the acceptance of deposits.

Overseas Cotton Market Snippets 183

American New Cotton News Favorable Yesterday, the American cotton market opened quietly. Liverpool news was unfavorable. Local and Liverpool parties sold, and each month's price fell by 1 to 8 points. Trading was light, and buyers were discouraged. Although the stock market rose in the afternoon, it was not enough to trigger new purchases. The market is currently stagnant. Cotton harvest and weather news are favorable. Finally, the market price fell again due to sales from local and New Orleans parties. The market stabilized before closing. Spot prices fell by 10 points, and futures prices fell by 8 to 13 points. English cotton spot prices fell by 2 points, and futures prices rose by 1 point. Indian cotton saw short covering and speculative buying, while operators took profits on long positions. Pitgole rose by half a rupee, Oomra rose by 1.5 rupees, and White Row Key rose by 1.25 rupees. The original telegram is recorded on the left (dated July 29th):

Grains Thin Rice Arrivals, Prices Fall, Eastern New Rice 1 Yuan Lower than Initial Opening Price 184

Local Rice (South Shanghai): Yesterday, rice market arrivals were all thin rice, accounting for thirteen or fourteen, with a total of nearly three thousand piculs. Therefore, although the Tianjin group undertook to buy 500 to 600 packages of thin rice, the situation eventually softened, and prices fell by more than one corner. As for Su Tong Japonica and South Port early rice, fortunately, there were no arrivals, so although sales in this street were weak, the market price was still able to stabilize. The supply and demand are similar to the original market, and there is no prosperity or decline in the market. Lu Jian rice is quite popular due to several days of out of stock. Dong Xin rice is selling at two corners, with the price opening at ten yuan, which is one yuan lower compared to the initial opening price. (North Shanghai) Yesterday, there were fourteen or fifteen ships from various sources downstream. Various types of white Japonica rice in the market were average, and the price trend was stable with a slight fatigue. Dong Xin Japonica rice had a strong trading volume, about two hundred or more piculs. Retail sales were sluggish, and the price was fatigued by two corners. Scattered transactions of white yuan continued to take place, and the price trend increased slightly by a corner. Gao Yang Jian rice was priced up by two corners due to its scarcity. The other types of rice were neither prosperous nor declining.

Foreign Rice: Yesterday, the sales volume of this rice by local customers had decreased. 5,800 bags of Saigon rice and 700 bags of Siamese rice with small strands were offered for sale all day, with a total transaction of less than 7,000 bags. As customer demand was weak, the market seemed to have a tendency to decline. However, both buyers and sellers were unwilling to let go easily, as the current inventory had decreased, and rumors of the silver issue and inflation were rampant, so they were even more unwilling to sell. Since the sellers insisted on not selling, the market then tended to stabilize again, and the later trend turned strong.

Excitement High, Flour and Wheat Become Expensive 185

Flour Market: The distant futures market is once again showing an upward trend. Foreign wheat is reportedly up two corners in Chicago and up eight cents in Canada. At the time of opening prices, because this month is the last day, both buyers and sellers were engaged in closing out positions, so only in the three or four sessions did it rise by one point, and then it returned to flat. As for the various future months, due to the increasing rumors of inflation and the gradual rise in the price of gold, as well as the silver issue, the sentiment both inside and outside the industry is uniformly good. The buying interest is particularly strong, and the transaction volume has reached more than 700,000 packages. Large factories are still engaged in hedging sales, with a quantity of about 100,000 or more. However, the sentiment is still developing, and the market atmosphere has not been hit. Before the pros and cons of the inflation issue are clarified, it seems to be beneficial to the good prices of goods. As a result, this month is unchanged, August rose by 1.75 points, September rose by 1.5 points, October rose by 2.75 points, and November rose by point.

Wheat: Yesterday, the futures market for all months showed a frantic upward trend. Although foreign wheat prices were up by only eight cents to one corner, the market sentiment was extremely excited. Industry insiders believed that the current wheat prices were very high, and the prices in various producing areas were also rising. Therefore, the opening prices were already strong. In the middle of the day, due to the rise in the flour market and the increasing rumors of inflation, buyers both inside and outside the industry were extremely enthusiastic, and the market rose step by step. As a result, each month showed a huge increase of up to one corner and one point, and the total increase also reached nine points to one corner. In this situation, it seems to be completely dominated by inflation rumors. As a result, August rose by one corner, September rose by one corner and one point, and October and November each rose by nine points. Spot wheat also rose by three to five points due to customer sales. However, in terms of the high-end goods, it has secretly risen nearly a corner. The opening price of Yangzhou wheat is 3.48 yuan, and the secondary wheat is 4.5 points, Zhenjiang wheat is 3.435 yuan, Shandong Yaowan Yanghe wheat is 3.62 yuan, Gaozi wheat is 3.478 yuan, Luhe Sixhe wheat is 3.5 yuan, Wuhe Sizhou wheat is 3.54 yuan, and Jiangbei wheat is 3.52 yuan. Fuxin shipped 7,500 packages, and Shenda shipped 1,000 packages.

Free Talk

"Words of Warning in a Prosperous Age" 188

— Cao Juren

In the late Qing Dynasty, Tang Shoupeng of Shanyin, Zhejiang, once published a book called *Words of Warning in a Prosperous Age*. I was very young when I read that book, and now my impression is vague. The year before last, I saw something similar to *Words of Warning in a Prosperous Age* sent from Guangzhou; it worried that a great disaster of national subjugation and racial extinction was imminent, urging the people of the country to be vigilant and strive early. It was the heartfelt words of a concerned person. Among the people of the country, there were certainly those who were fearful, like Huang Zunxian (Gongdu), who wrote such poems after the Sino-Japanese War:

"Since abandoning Zhuyai, everyone has followed suit. Partitioning is only heard by guests, and when the fuel is exhausted, they turn to me for help.

In the days of Qin and Chu's diplomacy, the Sixteen Prefectures of You and Yan were lost. Never have I heard of the Northern and Southern Seas being everywhere choked.

The weak are preyed upon by the strong, everyone is in the tiger's mouth; the boundless map is divided, and all the land is leaving China.

Who cares about the Three Kingdoms, with the cross flag spread everywhere. Poland and India, who knows what the future holds?"

Decades have passed, and we have never tasted the great pain of racial extinction; national subjugation, as expected, does not necessarily involve great hardship, and most people can still live happy and bustling lives. Some people think of the "Words of Warning in a Prosperous Age" as a prediction like "a comet's tail sweeps across the Earth, and the Earth will be destroyed," treating it as a foreign tale and "listening to it just for fun."

During the reign of Emperor Wen of the Western Han Dynasty, there was a scholar named Jia Yi who was favored by Emperor Wen. When he made recommendations, Emperor Wen would listen attentively, but Jia Sheng's petitions and strategies were always accompanied by weeping and long sighs. Even with an enlightened ruler like Emperor Wen, Jia Sheng's weeping and long sighs were the words of warning for a prosperous era. Jia Sheng himself seemed very frustrated, crossing the Miluo River to mourn Qu Yuan, and later dying young from grief. Compared to another scholar who wept and sighed—Yuan Ang, who, by helping the emperor to eliminate the imperial clan, provoked the disaster of the Seven Kingdoms Rebellion and became a sacrifice to the slogan of "clearing the emperor's court"—Jia Sheng's words of warning were much more fortunate. Only in a prosperous era can there be words of warning, and only with an enlightened ruler like Emperor Wen could Jia Sheng's weeping and sighing avoid causing offense; prudence is the way to protect oneself, and the sages have given us a clever method. In the late Eastern Han Dynasty, the prohibitions against party members lasted for more than twenty years, and thousands of scholar-officials were killed and imprisoned. Later, the eunuch Lü Qiang told Emperor Ling of Han: "The prohibitions against party members have accumulated for a long time, and people are full of resentment. If they are not pardoned soon, they may conspire with Zhang Jiao, and the trouble will become greater, and it will be too late to regret." Emperor Ling became afraid and lifted the ban on party members. Soon after, the Yellow Turban Rebellion broke out, and the Eastern Han Dynasty came to an end. At that time, there was a scholar named Zhongchang Tong, who always sighed with indignation when discussing current affairs. His book *Chang Yan* denounced the government where "rulers and ministers indulge in licentiousness, and superiors and inferiors share the same evil," and attacked the powerful clans with "hundreds of interconnected buildings and fields full of fertile land," predicting the end of the Han Dynasty. This was also a Jia Sheng-style warning of weeping and sighing, and it was expected that it would be resented by the times; however, his own attitude was very passive, only wanting to live a reclusive life where he had "good fields and spacious houses, backing onto mountains and facing streams, surrounded by ditches and pools, with bamboo and trees all around, a threshing ground in front, and an orchard behind, with boats and carriages sufficient to replace the difficulty of walking, and servants sufficient to relieve the labor of the four limbs, nourishing parents with delicacies, and wives and children without the hardship of physical labor; when good friends come to visit, serving wine and delicacies to entertain them, and on auspicious days, slaughtering lamb and pork to offer." He was satisfied with this, so even though he spoke out boldly, he had no major worries.

Writing this, I am reminded of another kind of words of warning in a prosperous age. At the turn of the Ming and Qing Dynasties, the great scholar Huang Zongxi of the Southeast wrote a book called *Mingyi Daifang Lu* (*A Plan for the Prince*), of which only a thin volume remains. We speculate that the original book was at least four or five times larger than the existing one; these missing parts were all deleted by the enlightened rulers of the early Qing Dynasty, Kangxi, Yongzheng, and Qianlong; the "Ten-Complete Emperor" who revered antiquity and valued literature subjected *Mingyi Daifang Lu* to a slow and painful execution. Huang Zongxi believed that Jizi presented the *Hong Fan* (Grand Norm) and King Wu listened attentively; his *Daifang Lu* would one day see the light of day. Little did he expect that later King Wus would want Confucius to delete the *Book of Songs* and mutilate the *Hong Fan*. Therefore, words of warning can only be spoken in a vague way; if they are to be as specific as in *Mingyi Daifang Lu*, one can only follow Sima Qian's method of storing them in famous mountains and passing them on to the right person.

Someone said: Isn't Han Feizi's *Signs of Ruin* an even more specific words of warning in a prosperous age? Han Feizi listed forty-seven signs of ruin (signs of ruin do not necessarily mean inevitable ruin, but indicate the possibility of ruin). Among them, the most essential are: "If ministers study, disciples are fond of arguing, merchants accumulate wealth abroad, and the common people are in internal distress, the state can be ruined. If people rely on auspicious days, serve ghosts and gods, believe in divination, and are fond of sacrifices, the state can be ruined. If people are fond of cruel punishments and do not adhere to the law, like to argue without seeking practical use, and indulge in flowery writing without regard for its effectiveness, the state can be ruined. If people rely on foreign aid and neglect their neighbors, and rely on the help of powerful states and despise the countries they oppress, the state can be ruined. If people like to use cleverness to circumvent the law, often mix private interests with public affairs, frequently change laws and prohibitions, and issue orders repeatedly, the state can be ruined. If the command of armies and the appointment of generals are too important, and the defense of the borders is entrusted to high-ranking officials, who act arbitrarily and make decisions without seeking permission, the state can be ruined. If people see great benefits but do not pursue them, hear of dangers but do not prepare for them, are shallow in matters of defense, and try to adorn themselves with benevolence and righteousness, the state can be ruined." Later, the state of Han was indeed ruined by these, and other states like Chu, Qi, Yan, and Zhao were also ruined by these. Han Feizi's words were all unfortunately accurate. Before Qu Yuan drowned himself in the Miluo River, he could still write a long *Nine Chapters* and short, satisfying articles to vent his grievances, while Han Feizi's forty-seven signs of ruin can be completely preserved to this day. If he had lived in the era of the Ten-Complete Emperor who revered antiquity and valued literature, could Han Feizi have avoided the fate of *Mingyi Daifang Lu*?

The above are all old stories from the past.

Science Is Not a Docile Child 189

— Te

The progress of science is becoming faster and faster. From primitive humans to Hesiod, the Greek poet, it was about 50,000 years or more. From Hesiod to Leonardo da Vinci, it was about 2,500 years. From da Vinci to Benjamin Franklin, it was 350 years. From Franklin to today, it has been 150 years. The achievements of each era are always much richer than those of the previous era.

Humanity itself is still very young, but science is still in its infancy. Our knowledge is like a ball, and everything we learn is built on the surface of the ball. What we do not know is the space outside the ball—boundless.

Science from thirty years ago is now obsolete. Old science libraries are simply large piles of dead facts, covered in dust, with no one asking about them, but this neglect is often too much.

Scientists are the noblest kind of people, they not only seek realization, but also add some light to the future of mankind.

The struggle of mankind today is a war of conquest. We must strive to overcome the forces of nature and utilize them. But to know oneself and one's enemy is to win every battle. Therefore, if we want to win, we must first know them. If we do not know where the enemy is, where do we start the attack?

The greatest tool of science is the human brain. Intelligence is more important and more powerful than telescopes, microscopes, and galvanometers. The spirit of creation flourishes endlessly, so the hope for the progress of science is almost infinite.

Science is not limited by time, does not belong to any one country, does not belong to any one continent, does not belong to any one century, does not even belong to this world, nor does it belong to the solar system, but it belongs to the universe.

We may think that scientists and ordinary people behave differently, but this is a misconception. Scientists are also people, often very ordinary people, but their work exceeds the efforts of other people. If you want to despise science, you must be careful, because behind it lies permanent, unlimited power, and creation.

The work of art, no matter how admirable, is only a reflection of an ideal. Science offers us fragments of reality. In other words, art is human, science is superhuman.

Scientists have inventors, critics, and scholars of various kinds. These people each have their own characteristics. A true scientist can melt these many characteristics into one, but they are rarely combined in one person. Scientists focus on research, sometimes emphasizing one aspect and sometimes lacking other aspects.

Invention comes from perseverance. Famous scientists all have great and glorious tenacity.

Self-confidence is the most needed by scientists. When he enters the laboratory, he must have the belief and the enthusiasm of a Christian martyr.

There are several great inventions in the world that were not made by scientists. Such as the English physician Jenner's invention of the smallpox vaccine, the French physician Laennec's invention of diagnostics. Also, the French diplomat Lesseps was not an engineer, but his successful career surpassed the work of hundreds of capable engineers. (Note: Lesseps was the planner of the Suez Canal).

The ideal scientist has no other desires besides his scientific research and does not care about the gain or loss of power. He spends his precious time in the laboratory, surrounded only by three or four students who are dedicated to learning. Every day when he comes out of the laboratory, his mind is always filled with creative dreams. In front of him, there is always a light like a bright star, guiding him to a new invention, large or small.

Now, many complete laboratories have been built in various countries, with bright electric lights and sophisticated and strange instruments. But Lavoisier (French chemist, improved the method of making gunpowder, discovered the composition of air, and clarified the properties of oxygen), Pasteur (French chemist and microscope scholar, discovered the principle of fermentation, and studied the rabies vaccination treatment), Curie (French chemist, discovered radium), and many other workers all completed their great inventions in poor and humble houses.

Science is not a docile and polite child who is satisfied with some comfort and love. It is harsh, cold, and merciless, and is often willing to make great sacrifices over the years for a very small hobby.

The greatest inventions can be summed up in a short phrase. Lavoisier said: "Life is a chemical phenomenon." Pasteur determined that all diseases are caused by parasites. Chemistry, physics, and medicine are nothing more than the development of these two themes.

Blind suspicion and blind faith come from the same source. Believing without any evidence and not believing any evidence are equally foolish.

A true scientist must dare to be revolutionary. He must also hold a skeptical attitude towards the most respected theories. He must discuss everything, he must closely study everything. Scientific thought comes from curiosity, medical thought is in the pursuit of safety. But the safety of doctors must be based on the curiosity of scientists.

There is a kind of academic system in science, everything is fine and extremely fine. But the historical and descriptive sciences have a range that is much narrower than that of experimental science. Chemistry and physics have now surpassed everything. Physics can give us insight into the properties of all things.

This history of science is a history of mistakes. Some of these mistakes are very large, and sometimes extremely ridiculous. But on the whole, the losses of the former are the teachers of the latter, and their mistakes are also beneficial to people.

Since Lavoisier, there is no longer any doubt that life can be scientifically produced. But this burning of all life is not the only purpose of life. It cannot be believed that creation patiently creates countless organisms, giving them different shapes and sophisticated and complex machines, solely for the purpose of producing more heat, water, and carbonic acid. Therefore, the chemical force of the living world must become a tool, but not a result.

Diligent work is not enough to make a great invention, and even a small invention will not be made because of it. Many warriors have lived the diligent life of scientists, but what have they achieved? They have failed both opportunity and wisdom.

The history of science proves that, with the exception of mathematics, all progress cannot be achieved solely through theories inspired by libraries or research institutes. It is necessary to constantly observe and constantly experiment to achieve progress.

An experiment, no matter how clumsy the plan is, or how clumsy the implementation, is more valuable than a bright theory.

Future inventions are endless, and countless treasures are buried in everything hidden.

University Days (III) (IV) 190

— Written by the German writer Storm, translated by Chen Yinzhi

"So I went to her house, and as I expected, I met her in a side room in her aunt's house, where her housekeeping was. She was standing in the middle of the room, her face pale, her teeth biting her lips, biting them until blood flowed down. All the drawers and boxes were opened by her; lace and pieces of cloth were scattered all over the floor around. 'Nali!' I shouted, 'What are you doing, Nali?' But she seemed not to hear me. — 'Is there dancing in the dance hall on Sunday?' she asked. 'Dance hall? — What does that have to do with you!' — 'I want to go dancing!' — 'You? What would your sweetheart say?' — 'What does my sweetheart have to do with me!' — At this time, she had already put on her hat and taken out her scarf from the wardrobe. Then she opened a small box, in which she usually kept the money she had saved; — although she usually liked to spend money on decorations, she always saved some money so that she would not go to her bridegroom's house naked. Now she tore open the paper package and put the money in her pocket. 'Are you coming with me?' she asked, but she insisted that I go, so I followed her, because I still hoped to dissuade her from dancing. But my words were all in vain, because she hurried along the street with me, neither listening to a word I said nor looking at me.

"When we walked into the market and stood in front of the cloth shop counter, she called the shop assistant to bring out the best-looking silk and the most fashionable brocade gauze to look at, which she usually only saw in the houses of the noblest people in the city. She searched among them, making a mess of things. The shop assistant also took out a piece of goods. 'If the lady who buys the flower material can afford the price...!' he said, putting his hand under this transparent material. 'It doesn't matter,' Nali said, 'she can afford the price'. — I secretly touched her, because I now understood that she was going to buy this expensive material for herself. 'Nali,' I said softly, 'I ask you to think again, what do you want this expensive thing for?' — But she paid no attention, she called the shop assistant to cut the material, and counted the shiny money on the counter. She seemed not to think about how much sweat she had shed to earn this money. 'Don't mind me,' she said, when I kept pulling her arm, 'I always want to wear good clothes once, I am not uglier than the most beautiful girl here!'"

Sleepless Night (Part 2) 191

— Long Zaitian

Space expanded infinitely, and time gradually passed. Kang Yu and Meina's breathing gradually made him jealous; and the sound of the wind in the tops of the poplar trees grew tighter and tighter, causing the two windows to rattle, making the late night even more eerie and frightening; the sound of the chain on the wall that broke through the silence insisted on chiming twice... Liangfu then deliberately turned over hard, making his bed vibrate to boost his courage. But after a moment of calm, the wounds that life had given him, the pale face of his mother who had encountered unexpected misfortune, crept like insects onto his swollen meninges.

First, countless sparks burst out in his eyes. These countless sparks condensed into the pale face of his mother. Her sparse, gray hair swayed weakly; in her sunken eye sockets, few eyelashes were covered with lonely tears, which dripped down, wetting her thin face completely.

Suddenly, the drooping top of the bed transformed into a huge Western-style building. Then, in a dizzying manner, all the outlines blurred and magnified. His body seemed to have been transported to a newly built, exquisite Western-style house, and a middle-aged man wearing black tortoiseshell-rimmed glasses kept saying to him:

"We are looking for people based on the work, not looking for work based on the people. If two people or one person can do the job, we will never add another. We never have anyone idle..."

After hearing this unnecessary "official talk," he couldn't help feeling indignant and planned to reply to the middle-aged man forcefully, but he couldn't make a sound. It turned out that the quilt was pressing on his upper chest, and everything was quiet. So Liangfu pushed the quilt away a little and turned over again.

The clock on the wall, clearly and as if to warn him especially, forcefully struck four times! The summer night was short, and the eastern glass window had already let in the light of dawn. The broken-legged stool, the messy pile on the table, the kerosene lamp with the broken bulb, and the bottles and jars all revealed their hazy lines. This, in turn, caused Liangfu to feel a strong sense of irritation; especially after the recurrence of the mole on the edge of his eyelid, he felt a spasm-like tremor; finally, it made him attempt to use extremely base methods to induce sleep.

Perhaps it was truly effective? He fell asleep hazily. But after a short while, he woke up with a loud shout.

"What's wrong? Liangfu, don't scare me to death!" The lively Kang Yu was the first to ask him.

Liangfu was also awake at this time, knowing that it was the customary sleep paralysis, but he was very embarrassed to receive Kang Yu's question, and instead held his breath, not daring to move at all, pretending that nothing had happened. It wasn't until Kang Yu's snoring resumed that he grandly turned over. Before long, a messy sound of footsteps came, which made him unable to sleep peacefully anymore. Liangfu then reluctantly hugged his sore and thin legs, carried his rather heavy and swollen head, and climbed out of bed.

Aceh Night 192

— Hei Ying

The sky is full of stars shining

Like countless angry eyes,

Staring at the pitch-black

Aceh prairie.

The surrounding silence suddenly came

The shouts of the waves,

A fire lit in the coconut grove,

Burn—I am waiting for the prairie fire

Once flowed with bright red blood,

Painted as one side of colonial history.

Aceh—

I serve a tomorrow with you.

Shatter the shackles on your body,

And rush through this endless darkness.

When the rising sun rises in the east,

We will read for freedom.
